19:01:33","updatedTime":"2020-08-16 19:01:33","title":"Announcing General Availability of HDInsight on Linux + new Data Lake Services and Language","link":"https://weblogs.asp.net:443/scottgu/announcing-general-availability-of-hdinsight-on-linux-new-data-lake-services-and-language","description":"<p>Today, I’m happy to announce several key additions to our big data services in Azure, including the General Availability of HDInsight on Linux, as well as the introduction of our new Azure Data Lake and Language services. <h2><u>General Availability of HDInsight on Linux </u></h2> <p>Today we are announcing general availability of our HDInsight service on Ubuntu Linux.&nbsp; HDInsight enables you to easily run managed Hadoop clusters in the cloud.&nbsp; With today’s release we now allow you to configure these clusters to run using both a Windows Server Operating System as well as an Ubuntu based Linux Operating System. <p>HDInsight on Linux enables even broader support for <a href=\"http://azure.microsoft.com/blog/2015/07/15/azure-hdinsight-launches-isv-partner-program-at-wpc/\"> Hadoop ecosystem partners</a> to run in HDInsight providing you even greater choice of preferred tools and applications for running Hadoop workloads. Both Linux and Windows clusters in HDInsight are built on the same standard Hadoop distribution and offer the same set of rich capabilities.  <p>Today’s new release also enables additional capabilities, such as, <a href=\"https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/documentation/articles/hdinsight-hadoop-linux-information/#scaling\">cluster scaling</a>, <a href=\"https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/documentation/articles/hdinsight-extend-hadoop-virtual-network/\">virtual network integration</a> and <a href=\"https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/documentation/articles/hdinsight-hadoop-customize-cluster-linux/\">script action support</a>. Furthermore, in addition to Hadoop cluster type, you can now create <a href=\"https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/documentation/articles/hdinsight-hbase-tutorial-get-started-linux\">HBase</a> and <a href=\"https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/documentation/articles/hdinsight-apache-storm-tutorial-get-started-linux/\">Storm</a> clusters on Linux for your NoSQL and real time processing needs such as <a href=\"https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/documentation/articles/hdinsight-storm-develop-java-event-hub-topology/\">building an IoT application</a>. <p><strong><em>Create a cluster</em></strong></p> <p>HDInsight clusters running using Linux can now be easily created from the <a href=\"https://portal.azure.com/\">Azure Management portal</a> under the Data + Analytics section.&nbsp; Simply select Ubuntu from the cluster operating system drop-down, as well as optionally choose the cluster type you wish to create (we support base Hadoop as well as clusters pre-configured for workloads like Storm, Spark, HBase, etc). <p><a href=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/Windows-Live-Writer/3d66647f8083_97AD/image_2.png\"><img title=\"image\" style=\"border-top: 0px; border-right: 0px; background-image: none; border-bottom: 0px; padding-top: 0px; padding-left: 0px; border-left: 0px; display: inline; padding-right: 0px\" border=\"0\" alt=\"image\" src=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/Windows-Live-Writer/3d66647f8083_97AD/image_thumb.png\" width=\"823\" height=\"536\"></a> <p>All HDInsight Linux clusters can be managed by Apache Ambari. Ambari provides the ability to customize configuration settings of your Hadoop cluster while giving you a unified view of the performance and state of your cluster and providing monitoring and alerting within the HDInsight cluster. <p><a href=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/Windows-Live-Writer/3d66647f8083_97AD/image_6.png\"><img title=\"image\" style=\"border-top: 0px; border-right: 0px; background-image: none; border-bottom: 0px; padding-top: 0px; padding-left: 0px; border-left: 0px; display: inline; padding-right: 0px\" border=\"0\" alt=\"image\" src=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/Windows-Live-Writer/3d66647f8083_97AD/image_thumb_2.png\" width=\"896\" height=\"504\"></a> <p><strong><em>Installing additional applications and Hadoop components</em></strong></p> <p>Similar to HDInsight Windows clusters, you can now customize your Linux cluster by installing additional applications or Hadoop components that are not part of default HDInsight deployment. This can be accomplished using Bash scripts with <a href=\"https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/documentation/articles/hdinsight-hadoop-customize-cluster-linux/\">script action</a> capability.&nbsp; As an example, you can now <a href=\"http://go.microsoft.com/fwlink/?LinkId=623221\">install Hue on an HDInsight Linux cluster</a> and easily use it with your workloads: <p><a href=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/Windows-Live-Writer/3d66647f8083_97AD/image_10.png\"><img title=\"image\" style=\"border-top: 0px; border-right: 0px; background-image: none; border-bottom: 0px; padding-top: 0px; padding-left: 0px; border-left: 0px; display: inline; padding-right: 0px\" border=\"0\" alt=\"image\" src=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/Windows-Live-Writer/3d66647f8083_97AD/image_thumb_4.png\" width=\"845\" height=\"515\"></a> <p><strong><em>Develop using Familiar Tools </em></strong></p> <p>All HDInsight Linux clusters come with SSH connectivity enabled by default. You can connect to the cluster via a SSH client of your choice. Moreover, SSH tunneling can be leveraged to remotely access all of the Hadoop web applications from the browser.  <p><a href=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/Windows-Live-Writer/3d66647f8083_97AD/image_8.png\"><img title=\"image\" style=\"border-top: 0px; border-right: 0px; background-image: none; border-bottom: 0px; padding-top: 0px; padding-left: 0px; border-left: 0px; display: inline; padding-right: 0px\" border=\"0\" alt=\"image\" src=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/Windows-Live-Writer/3d66647f8083_97AD/image_thumb_3.png\" width=\"624\" height=\"424\"></a> <h2><u>New Azure Data Lake Services and Language</u></h2> <p>We continue to see customers enabling amazing scenarios with big data in Azure including <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=vCC44qnwLF0\">analyzing social graphs</a> to increase charitable giving, <a href=\"https://customers.microsoft.com/Pages/CustomerStory.aspx?recid=21129\">analyzing radiation exposure</a> and using the signals from thousands of devices to simulate ways for utility customers to optimize their monthly bills. These and other use cases are resulting in even more data being collected in Azure. In order to be able to dive deep into all of this data, and process it in different ways, you can now use our Azure Data Lake capabilities – which are 3 services that make big data easy.  <p>The first service in the family is available today: Azure HDInsight, our managed Hadoop service that lets you focus on finding insights, and not spend your time having to manage clusters. HDInsight lets you deploy Hadoop, Spark, Storm and HBase clusters, running on Linux or Windows, managed, monitored and supported by Microsoft with a 99.9% SLA.  <p>The other two services, Azure Data Lake Store and Azure Data Lake Analytics introduced below, are available in private preview today and will be available broadly for public usage shortly. <h2><u>Azure Data Lake Store</u></h2> <p>Azure Data Lake Store is a hyper-scale HDFS repository designed specifically for big data analytics workloads in the cloud. Azure Data Lake Store solves the big data challenges of volume, variety, and velocity by enabling you to store data of any type, at any size, and process it at any scale. Azure Data Lake Store can support near real-time scenarios such as the Internet of Things (IoT) as well as throughput-intensive analytics on huge data volumes. The Azure Data Lake Store also supports a variety of computation workloads by removing many of the restrictions constraining traditional analytics infrastructure like the pre-definition of schema and the creation of multiple data silos. Once located in the Azure Data Lake Store, Hadoop-based engines such as Azure HDInsight can easily mine the data to discover new insights. <p>Some of the key capabilities of Azure Data Lake Store include: <ul> <li><b>Any Data</b>: A distributed file store that allows you to store data in its native format, Azure Data Lake Store eliminates the need to transform or pre-define schema in order to store data.</li> <li><b>Any Size: </b>With no fixed limits to file or account sizes, Azure Data Lake Store enables you to store kilobytes to exabytes with immediate read/write access.</li> <li><b>At Any Scale: </b>You can scale throughput to meet the demands of your analytic systems including the high throughput needed to analyze exabytes of data. In addition, it is built to handle high volumes of small writes at low latency making it optimal for near real-time scenarios like website analytics, and Internet of Things (IoT).</li> <li><b>HDFS Compatible</b>: It works out-of-the-box with the Hadoop ecosystem including other Azure Data Lake services such as HDInsight.</li> <li><b>Fully Integrated with Azure Active Directory: </b>Azure Data Lake Store is integrated with Azure Active Directory for identity and access management over all of your data.</li></ul> <h2><u>Azure Data Lake Analytics with U-SQL</u></h2> <p>The new Azure Data Lake Analytics service makes it much easier to create and manage big data jobs. Built on YARN and years of experience running analytics pipelines for Office 365, XBox Live, Windows and Bing, the Azure Data Lake Analytics service is the most productive way to get insights from big data. You can get started in the <a href=\"https://portal.azure.com/\">Azure management portal,</a> querying across data in blobs, Azure Data Lake Store, and Azure SQL DB. By simply moving a slider, you can scale up as much computing power as you’d like to run your data transformation jobs.  <p><a href=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/Windows-Live-Writer/3d66647f8083_97AD/image_12.png\"><img title=\"image\" style=\"border-top: 0px; border-right: 0px; background-image: none; border-bottom: 0px; padding-top: 0px; padding-left: 0px; border-left: 0px; display: inline; padding-right: 0px\" border=\"0\" alt=\"image\" src=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/Windows-Live-Writer/3d66647f8083_97AD/image_thumb_5.png\" width=\"885\" height=\"510\"></a> <p>Today we are introducing a new <a href=\"http://blogs.msdn.com/b/visualstudio/archive/2015/09/28/introducing-u-sql.aspx\">U-SQL offering</a> in the analytics service, an evolution of the familiar syntax of SQL.&nbsp; U-SQL allows you to write declarative big data jobs, as well as easily include your own user code as part of those jobs. Inside Microsoft, developers have been using this combination in order to be productive operating on massive data sets of many exabytes of scale, processing mission critical data pipelines. In addition to providing an easy to use experience in the Azure management portal, we are delivering a rich set of tools in Visual Studio for debugging and optimizing your U-SQL jobs. This lets you play back and analyze your big data jobs, understanding bottlenecks and opportunities to improve both performance and efficiency, so that you can pay only for the resources you need and continually tune your operations. <p><a href=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/Windows-Live-Writer/3d66647f8083_97AD/image_14.png\"><img title=\"image\" style=\"border-top: 0px; border-right: 0px; background-image: none; border-bottom: 0px; padding-top: 0px; padding-left: 0px; border-left: 0px; display: inline; padding-right: 0px\" border=\"0\" alt=\"image\" src=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/Windows-Live-Writer/3d66647f8083_97AD/image_thumb_6.png\" width=\"845\" height=\"540\"></a> <h2><u>Learn More</u></h2> <p>For more information and to get started, check out the following links: <ul> <li><a href=\"https://technet.microsoft.com/en-us/dn282640\">Sign up for the Azure Data Lake Store and Analytics services preview</a> <li><a href=\"http://www.azure.com/datalake\">Azure Data Lake</a> <li><a href=\"http://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/services/hdinsight/\">Azure HDInsight</a> <li><a 19:01:33","updatedTime":"2020-08-16 19:01:33","title":"New Azure Billing APIs Available","link":"https://weblogs.asp.net:443/scottgu/new-azure-billing-apis-available","description":"<p>Organizations moving to the cloud can achieve significant cost savings.&nbsp; But to achieve the maximum benefit you need to be able to accurately track your cloud spend in order to monitor and predict your costs. Enterprises need to be able to get detailed, granular consumption data and derive insights to effectively manage their cloud consumption.  <p>I’m excited to announce the public preview release of two new Azure Billing APIs today: the <a href=\"https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/documentation/articles/billing-usage-rate-card-overview/\"><b>Azure Usage API</b> and <b>Azure RateCard API</b></a><b> </b>which provide customers and partners programmatic access to their Azure consumption and pricing details:  <p> <blockquote> <p><b>Azure Usage API</b> – A REST API that customers and partners can use to get their usage data for an Azure subscription. As part of this new Billing API we now correlate the usage/costs by the resource tags you can now set set on your Azure resources (for example: you could assign a tag “Department abc” or “Project X” to a VM or Database in order to better track spend on a resource and charge it back to an internal group within your company). To get more details, please read <a href=\"https://msdn.microsoft.com/en-us/library/azure/mt219001\">the MSDN page on the Usage API</a>. Enterprise Agreement (EA) customers can also use this API to get a more granular view into their consumption data, and to complement what they get from the EA Billing CSV. </p> <p><b>Azure RateCard API </b>– A REST API that customers and partners can use to get the list of the available resources they can use, along with metadata and price information about them. To get more details, please read <a href=\"https://msdn.microsoft.com/en-us/library/azure/mt219004\">the MSDN page on the RateCard API</a>. </p></blockquote> <p>You can start taking advantage of both of these APIs today.&nbsp; You can write your own custom code that uses the APIs to construct your own custom reports, or alternatively you can also now take advantage of pre-built bill tracking systems provided by our partners which already integrate the APIs into their existing solutions.</p> <h2><u>Partner Solutions</u></h2> <p>Two of our Azure Billing partners (<a href=\"https://www.cloudyn.com/microsoft-azure/\"><b>Cloudyn</b></a> and <a href=\"http://www.cloudcruiser.com/partners/microsoft/\"><b>Cloud Cruiser</b></a>) have already integrated the new Billing APIs into their products:  <blockquote> <p><b>Cloudyn</b> has integrated with Azure Billing APIs to provide IT financial management insights on cost optimization. You can read more about their integration experience in <a href=\"https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/documentation/articles/billing-usage-rate-card-partner-solution-cloudyn/\">Microsoft Azure Billing APIs enable Cloudyn to Provide ITFM for Customers</a>.  <p><b>Cloud Cruiser</b> has integrated with the Azure RateCard API to provide an estimate of what it would cost the customer to run the same workloads on Azure. They are also working on integrating with the Azure Usage API to provide insights based on the Azure consumption. You can read more about their integration in <a href=\"https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/documentation/articles/billing-usage-rate-card-partner-solution-cloudcruiser/\">Cloud Cruiser and Microsoft Azure Billing API Integration</a>. </p></blockquote> <p>You can adopt one or both of the above solutions immediately and use them to better track your Azure bill without having to write a single line of code.  <p><u></u></p> <p><a href=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/Windows-Live-Writer/abeb1f29193d_135B0/image_2.png\"><img title=\"image\" style=\"border-left-width: 0px; integration enables you to view and query the breakdown of Azure usage by resource tags (e.g. “Dev/Test”, “Department abc”, “Project X”):</p> <p><a href=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/Windows-Live-Writer/abeb1f29193d_135B0/image_4.png\"><img title=\"image\" style=\"border-left-width: 0px; border-right-width: 0px; background-image: none; border-bottom-width: 0px; padding-top: 0px; padding-left: 0px; margin: 15px 0px; display: inline; padding-right: 0px; border-top-width: 0px\" border=\"0\" alt=\"image\" estimated charges over time:</p> <p><a href=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/Windows-Live-Writer/abeb1f29193d_135B0/image_6.png\"><img title=\"image\" style=\"border-left-width: Cruiser's integration to show estimated cost of running workload on Azure:&nbsp;&nbsp; </p> <p><a src=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/Windows-Live-Writer/abeb1f29193d_135B0/image_thumb_3.png\" width=\"624\" height=\"338\"></a>  <h2><u>Using the Billing APIs directly</u></h2> <p>You can also use the new Billing APIs directly to write your own custom reports and billing tracking logic.&nbsp; To get started with the APIs, you can leverage the code samples <a href=\"https://github.com/Azure/BillingCodeSamples\">on Github</a>.  <p>The Billing APIs leverage the new Azure Resource Manager and use Azure Active Directory for Authentication and follow the Azure Role-based access control policies.&nbsp; The code samples we’ve published show a variety of common scenarios and how to integrate this logic end to end.  <h2><u>Summary</u></h2> <p>The new Azure Billing APIs make it much easier to track your bill and save money.  <p>As always, please reach out to us on the <a href=\"http://feedback.azure.com/forums/170030-billing\">Azure Feedback forum</a> Azure.&nbsp; Two weeks ago we <a href=\"http://weblogs.asp.net/scottgu/docker-and-microsoft-integrating-docker-with-windows-server-and-microsoft-azure\" target=\"_blank\">announced a partnership with Premium Storage offering (which will work with both our D-series and G-series of VMs) will support up to 32TB of storage per VM, &gt;50,000 IOPS of disk IO per VM, and enable sub-1ms read latency.&nbsp; Combined they provide an enormous amount of power that enables you to run even bigger and better solutions in the cloud.  <p>Earlier this week, we officially opened our new <a href=\"http://blogs.microsoft.com/blog/2014/10/26/microsoft-azure-australia-geo-generally-available/\" target=\"_blank\">Azure Australia regions</a> – which are our 18th and 19th Azure regions open for business around the world.&nbsp; Then at TechEd Europe we <a href=\"http://weblogs.asp.net/scottgu/azure-new-marketplace-network-improvements-new-batch-service-automation-service-more\" target=\"_blank\">announced another round of new features</a> – including the launch of the new <a href=\"http://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/marketplace/\" target=\"_blank\">Azure MarketPlace</a>, a bunch of great network improvements, our new <a href=\"http://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/services/batch/\" target=\"_blank\">Batch computing service</a>, general availability of our <a href=\"http://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/services/automation/\" target=\"_blank\">Azure Automation service</a> and more.  <p>Today, I’m excited to blog about even more new services we have released this week in the Azure Data space.&nbsp; These include: </p> <ul> <li><strong>Event Hubs:</strong> is a scalable service for ingesting and storing data from websites, client apps, and IoT sensors.  <li><strong>Stream Analytics</strong>: is a cost-effective event processing engine that helps uncover real-time insights from event streams.  <li><strong>Data Factory:</strong> enables better information production by orchestrating and managing diverse data and data movement. </li></ul> <p>Azure Event Hub is now available in general availability, and the new Azure Stream Analytics and Data Factory services are now in public preview.  <h2><u>Event Hubs: Log Millions of events per second in near real time</u></h2> <p>The <a href=\"http://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/services/event-hubs/\" target=\"_blank\">Azure Event Hub service</a> is a highly scalable telemetry ingestion service that can <strong>log millions of events per second</strong> in near real time.&nbsp; You can use the Event Hub service to collect data/events from any IoT device, from any app (web, mobile, or a backend service), or via feeds like social networks.&nbsp; We are using it internally within Microsoft to monitor some of our largest online systems.</p> <p>Once you collect events with Event Hub you can then analyze the data using any real-time analytics system (like Apache Storm or our new Azure Stream Analytics service) and store/transform it into any data storage system (including HDInsight and Hadoop based solutions).</p> <p>Event Hub is delivered as a managed service on Azure (meaning we run, scale and patch it for you and provide an enterprise SLA).&nbsp; It delivers:</p> <ul> <li>Ability to log millions of events per second in near real time  <li>Elastic scaling support with the ability to scale-up/down with no interruption  <li>Support for multiple protocols including support for HTTP and AMQP based events  <li>Flexible authorization and throttling device policies  <li>Time-based event buffering with event order preservation</li></ul> <p>The pricing model for Event Hubs is very flexible – for just $11/month you can provision a basic Event Hub with guaranteed performance capacity to capture 1 MB/sec of events sent to your Event Hub.&nbsp; You can then provision as many additional capacity units as you need if your event traffic goes higher.&nbsp; </p> <p><u><em>Getting Started with Capturing Events</em></u></p> <p>You can create a new Event Hub using the Azure Portal or via the command-line.&nbsp; Choose New-&gt;App Service-&gt;Service Bus-&gt;Event Hub in the portal to do so:</p> <p><a href=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/282efe892640_10ED0/image_2.png\"><img title=\"image\" style=\"border-left-width: 0px; border-right-width: 0px; border-bottom-width: 0px; display: inline; border-top-width: 0px\" border=\"0\" alt=\"image\" src=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/282efe892640_10ED0/image_thumb.png\" width=\"870\" height=\"327\"></a> </p> <p>Once created, events can be sent to an Event Hub with either a strongly-typed API (e.g. .NET or Java client library) or by just sending a raw HTTP or AMQP message to the service.&nbsp; Below is a simple example of how easy it is to log an IoT event to an Event Hub using just a standard HTTP post request.&nbsp; Notice the Authorization header in the HTTP post – you can use this to optionally enable flexible authentication/authorization for en\"><o:p></o:p></span></p></blockquote> <p>Your Event Hub can collect up to millions of messages per second like this, each storing whatever data schema you want within them, and the Event Hubs service will store them in-order for you to later read/consume. </p> <p><em><u>Downstream Event Processing</u></em></p> <p>Once you collect events, you no doubt want to do something with them.&nbsp; Event Hubs includes an intelligent processing agent that allows for automatic partition management and load distribution across readers.&nbsp; You can implement any logic you want within readers, and the data sent to the readers is delivered in the order it was sent to the Event Hub. </p> <p>In addition to supporting the ability for you to write custom Event Readers, we also have two easy ways to work with pre-built stream processing systems: including our new Azure Stream Analytics Service and Apache Storm.&nbsp; Our new Azure Stream Analytics service supports doing stream processing directly from Event Hubs, and Microsoft has created an Event Hubs Storm Spout for use with Apache Storm clusters.</p> <p>The below diagram helps express some of the many rich ways you can use Event Hubs to collect and then hand-off events/data for processing:</p> <p><a href=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/282efe892640_10ED0/image_8.png\"><img title=\"image\" style=\"border-left-width: 0px; border-right-width: 0px; border-bottom-width: 0px; display: inline; border-top-width: 0px\" border=\"0\" alt=\"image\" src=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/282efe892640_10ED0/image_thumb_3.png\" width=\"621\" height=\"297\"></a> </p> <p>Event Hubs provides a super flexible and cost effective building-block that you can use to collect and process any events or data you can stream to the cloud.&nbsp; It is very cost effective, and provides the scalability you need to meet any needs.</p> <p><u><em>Learning More about Event Hubs</em></u>  <p>For more information about Azure Event Hubs, please review the following resources:  <ul> <li><a href=\"http://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/services/event-hubs/\">Azure Event Hubs</a>  <li><a href=\"http://msdn.microsoft.com/en-us/library/azure/dn789972.aspx\">Event Hubs Conceptual Overview</a>  <li><a href=\"https://social.msdn.microsoft.com/Forums/azure/en-US/home?forum=servbus\">Azure Service Bus Forum</a>  <li><a href=\"http://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/documentation/articles/hdinsight-storm-sensor-data-analysis\">Storm Spout Resources</a>  <li><a href=\"http://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/services/stream-analytics/\">Azure Stream Analytics Resources</a></li></ul> <h2><u>Stream Analytics: Distributed Stream Processing Service for Azure</u></h2> <p>I’m excited to announce the preview our new Azure Stream Analytics service – a fully managed real-time distributed stream computation service that provides low latency, scalable processing of streaming data in the cloud with an enterprise grade SLA. The new Azure Stream Analytics service <strong>easily scales from small projects with just a few KB/sec of throughput to a</strong> <strong>gigabyte/sec or more of streamed data messages/events</strong>.&nbsp;&nbsp; <p>Our Stream Analytics pricing model enable you to run low throughput streaming workloads continuously at low cost, and enables you to only have to scale up as your business needs increase.&nbsp; We do this while maintaining built in guarantees of event delivery, and state management for fast recovery which enables mission critical business continuity.  <p><u><em>Dramatically Simpler Developer Experience for Stream Processing Data</em></u>  <p>Stream Analytics supports a SQL-like language that dramatically lowers the bar of the developer expertise required to create a scalable stream processing solution. A developer can simply write a few lines of SQL to do common operations including basic filtering, temporal analysis operations, joining multiple live streams of data with other static data sources, and detecting stream patterns (or lack thereof).  <p>This dramatically reduces the complexity and time it takes to develop, maintain and apply time-sensitive computations on real-time streams of data. Most other streaming solutions available today require you to write complex custom code, but with Azure Stream Analytics you can write simple, declarative and familiar SQL.  <p><u><em>Fully Managed Service that is Easy to Setup</em></u>  <p>With Stream Analytics you can dramatically accelerate how quickly you can derive valuable real time insights and analytics on data from devices, sensors, infrastructure, or applications. With a few clicks in the Azure Portal, you can create a streaming pipeline, configure its inputs and outputs, and provide SQL-like queries to describe the desired stream transformations/analysis you wish to do on the data. Once running, you are able to monitor the scale/speed of your overall streaming pipeline and make adjustments to achieve the desired throughput and latency.  <p>You can create a new Stream Analytics Job in the Azure Portal, by choosing <strong>New-&gt;Data Services-&gt;Stream Analytics</strong>:</p> <p><a href=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/282efe892640_10ED0/image_10.png\"><img title=\"image\" style=\"border-left-width: 0px; border-right-width: 0px; border-bottom-width: 0px; display: inline; border-top-width: 0px\" border=\"0\" alt=\"image\" src=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/282efe892640_10ED0/image_thumb_4.png\" width=\"624\" height=\"272\"></a> </p> <p><u><em>Setup Streaming Data Input</em></u></p> <p>Once created, your first step will be to add a Streaming Data Input.&nbsp; This allows you to indicate where the data you want to perform stream processing on is coming from.&nbsp; From within the portal you can choose <strong>Inputs-&gt;Add An Input </strong>to launch a wizard that enables you to specify this:</p> <p><a href=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/282efe892640_10ED0/image_12.png\"><img title=\"image\" style=\"border-left-width: 0px; border-right-width: 0px; border-bottom-width: 0px; display: inline; border-top-width: 0px\" border=\"0\" alt=\"image\" src=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/282efe892640_10ED0/image_thumb_5.png\" width=\"624\" height=\"264\"></a> </p> <p>We can use the Azure Event Hub Service to deliver us a stream of data to perform processing on. If you already have an Event Hub created, you can choose it from a list populated in the wizard above.&nbsp; You will also be asked to specify the format that is being used to serialize incoming event in the Event Hub (e.g. JSON, CSV or Avro formats).</p> <p><u><em>Setup Output Location</em></u></p> <p>The next step to developing our Stream Analytics job is to add a Streaming Output Location.&nbsp; This will configure where we want the output results of our stream processing pipeline to go.&nbsp; We can choose to easily output the results to Blob Storage, another Event Hub, or a SQL Database:</p> <p><a href=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/282efe892640_10ED0/image_16.png\"><img title=\"image\" style=\"border-left-width: 0px; border-right-width: 0px; border-bottom-width: 0px; display: inline; border-top-width: 0px\" border=\"0\" alt=\"image\" src=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/282efe892640_10ED0/image_thumb_7.png\" width=\"624\" height=\"232\"></a> </p> <p>Note that being able to use another Event Hub as a target provides a powerful way to connect multiple streams into an overall pipeline with multiple steps.</p> <p><u><em>Write Streaming Queries</em></u></p> <p>Now that we have our input and output sources configured, we can now write SQL queries to transform, aggregate and/or correlate the incoming input (or set of inputs in the event of multiple input sources) and output them to our output target.&nbsp; We can do this within the portal by selecting the <strong>QUERY</strong> tab at the top.</p> <p><a href=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/282efe892640_10ED0/image_14.png\"><img title=\"image\" style=\"border-left-width: 0px; border-right-width: 0px; border-bottom-width: 0px; display: inline; border-top-width: 0px\" border=\"0\" alt=\"image\" src=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/282efe892640_10ED0/image_thumb_6.png\" width=\"624\" height=\"94\"></a> </p> <p>There are a number of interesting queries you can write to processing the incoming stream of data.&nbsp; For example, in the previous Event Hub section of this blog post I showed how you can use an HTTP POST command to submit JSON based temperature data from an IoT device to an Event Hub with data in JSON format like so:</p> <blockquote> <p><span lang=\"EN\" style=\"font-size: 9pt; font-family: &quot;Courier New&quot;; color: black; mso-bidi-font-size: 10.0pt; mso-fareast-font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;; mso-ansi-language: en\">{ \"DeviceId\":\"dev-01\", \"Temperature\":\"37.0\" }</span></p></blockquote> <p>When multiple devices are streaming events simultaneously into our Event Hub like this, it would feed into our Stream Analytics job as a stream of continuous data events that look like the sequence below:</p> <p><img alt=\"\" src=\"https://acomdpsstorage.blob.core.windows.net/dpsmedia-prod/azure.microsoft.com/en-us/documentation/articles/stream-analytics-get-started/20141029115546/azurestreamanalyticssqloutput1.png\"></p> <p>Wouldn’t it be interesting to be able to analyze this data using a time-window perspective instead?&nbsp; For example, it would be useful to calculate in real-time what the average temperature of each device was in the last 5 seconds of multiple readings.</p> <p>With the Stream Analytics Service we can now dynamically calculate this over our incoming live stream of data just by writing a SQL query like so:</p> <form id=\"RunwayMasterForm\" method=\"post\"> <blockquote> <div class=\"wa-container\" data-tag-area=\"content\" data-tag-group=\"body\"><section class=\"wa-section class=\"pun\">.</span><span class=\"typ\">TimeStamp</span><span class=\"pun\">)</span><span class=\"pln\"> </span><span class=\"kwd\">as</span><span class=\"pln\"> </span><span class=\"typ\">WinStartTime</span><span class=\"pun\">,</span><span class=\"pln\"> system</span><span class=\"pun\">.</span><span class=\"typ\">TimeStamp</span><span class=\"pln\"> </span><span class=\"kwd\">as</span><span class=\"pln\"> </span><span class=\"typ\">WinEndTime</span><span class=\"pun\">,</span><span class=\"pln\"> </span><span class=\"typ\">DeviceId</span><span class=\"pun\">,</span><span class=\"pln\"> </span><span class=\"typ\">Avg</span><span class=\"pun\">(</span><span class=\"typ\">Temperature</span><span class=\"pun\">)</span><span class=\"pln\"> </span><span class=\"kwd\">as</span><span class=\"pln\"> </span><span class=\"typ\">AvgTemperature</span><span class=\"pun\">,</span><span class=\"pln\"> </span><span class=\"typ\">Count</span><span class=\"pun\">(*)</span><span class=\"pln\"> </span><span class=\"kwd\">as</span><span class=\"pln\"> </span><span class=\"typ\">EventCount</span><span class=\"pln\"> \n    FROM input\n    GROUP BY </span><span class=\"typ\">TumblingWindow</span><span class=\"pun\">(</span><span class=\"pln\">second</span><span class=\"pun\">,</span><span class=\"pln\"> </span><span class=\"lit\">5</span><span class=\"pun\">),</span><span class=\"pln\"> </span><span class=\"typ\">DeviceId</span><span class=\"pln\">\n</span></pre></div></section></div></blockquote></form>\n<p>Running this query in our Stream Analytics job will aggregate/transform our incoming stream of data events and output data like below into the output source we configured for our job (e,g, a blog storage file or a SQL Database):</p>\n<p><img alt=\"\" src=\"https://acomdpsstorage.blob.core.windows.net/dpsmedia-prod/azure.microsoft.com/en-us/documentation/articles/stream-analytics-get-started/20141029115546/azurestreamanalyticssqloutput2.png\"></p>\n<p>The great thing about this approach is that the data is being aggregated/transformed in real time as events are being streamed to us, and it scales to handle literally gigabytes of data event streamed per second.</p>\n<p><u><em>Scaling your Stream Analytics Job</em></u></p>\n<p>Once defined, you can easily monitor the activity of your Stream Analytics Jobs in the Azure Portal: </p>\n<p><a href=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/282efe892640_10ED0/image_20.png\"><img title=\"image\" style=\"border-left-width: 0px; border-right-width: 0px; border-bottom-width: 0px; display: inline; border-top-width: 0px\" border=\"0\" alt=\"image\" src=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/282efe892640_10ED0/image_thumb_9.png\" width=\"624\" height=\"282\"></a> </p>\n<p>You can use the <strong>SCALE</strong> tab to dynamically increase or decrease scale capacity for your stream processing – allowing you to pay only for the compute capacity you need, and enabling you to handle jobs with gigabytes/sec of streamed data.&nbsp; </p>\n<p><u><em>Learning More about Stream Analytics Service</em></u></p>\n<p>For more information about Stream Analytics, please review the following resources:</p>\n<ul>\n<li><a href=\"http://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/services/stream-analytics/\" target=\"_blank\">Stream Analytics Home Page</a> \n<li><a href=\"http://azure.microsoft.com/blog/2014/10/29/announcing-azure-stream-analytics-for-real-time-event-processing/\" target=\"_blank\">Blog Post Announcing Stream Analytics Preview</a> \n<li><a href=\"http://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/documentation/articles/stream-analytics-get-started/\" target=\"_blank\">Getting Started with Stream Analytics Tutorial</a> \n<li><a href=\"http://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/documentation/services/stream-analytics/\" target=\"_blank\">Stream Analytics Documentation</a></li></ul>\n<h2><u>Data Factory: Fully managed service to build and manage information production pipelines </u></h2>\n<p>Organizations are increasingly looking to fully leverage all of the data available to their business.&nbsp; As they do so, the data processing landscape is becoming more diverse than ever before – data is being processed across geographic locations, on-premises and cloud, across a wide variety of data types and sources (SQL, NoSQL, Hadoop, etc), and the volume of data needing to be processed is increasing exponentially. Developers today are often left writing large amounts of custom logic to deliver an information production system that can manage and co-ordinate all of this data and processing work. \n<p>To help make this process simpler, I’m excited to announce the preview of our new Azure Data Factory service – a fully managed service that makes it easy to compose data storage, processing, and data movement services into streamlined, scalable &amp; reliable data production pipelines. Once a pipeline is deployed, Data Factory enables easy monitoring and management of it, greatly reducing operational costs.&nbsp; <p><u><em>Easy to Get Started</em></u></p>\n<p>The Azure Data Factory is a fully managed service. Getting started with Data Factory is simple. With a few clicks in the <a href=\"https://portal.azure.com/\">Azure preview portal</a>, or via our command line operations, a developer can create a new data factory and link it to data and processing resources.&nbsp; From the new Azure Marketplace in the Azure Preview Portal, choose <strong>Data + Analytics –&gt; Data Factory</strong> to create a new instance in Azure:</p><a href=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/282efe892640_10ED0/image_24.png\"><img title=\"image\" style=\"border-left-width: 0px; border-right-width: 0px; border-bottom-width: 0px; display: inline; border-top-width: 0px\" border=\"0\" alt=\"image\" src=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/282efe892640_10ED0/image_thumb_11.png\" width=\"847\" height=\"491\"></a> \n<p><u><em>Orchestrating Information Production Pipelines across multiple data sources</em></u> \n<p>Data Factory makes it easy to coordinate and manage data sources from a variety of locations – including ones both in the cloud and on-premises.&nbsp; Support for working with data on-premises inside SQL Server, as well as Azure Blob, Tables, HDInsight Hadoop systems and SQL Databases is included in this week’s preview release.&nbsp; <p>Access to on-premises data is supported through a data management gateway that allows for easy configuration and management of secure connections to your on-premises SQL Servers.&nbsp; Data Factory balances the scale &amp; agility provided by the cloud, Hadoop and non-relational platforms, with the management &amp; monitoring that enterprise systems require to enable information production in a hybrid environment. \n<p><u><em>Custom Data Processing Activities using Hive, Pig and C#</em></u></p>\n<p>This week’s preview enables data processing using Hive, Pig and custom C# code activities.&nbsp; Data Factory activities can be used to clean data, anonymize/mask critical data fields, and transform the data in a wide variety of complex ways. </p>\n<p>The Hive and Pig activities can be run on an HDInsight cluster you create, or alternatively you can allow Data Factory to fully manage the Hadoop cluster lifecycle on your behalf.&nbsp; Simply author your activities, combine them into a pipeline, set an execution schedule and you’re done – no manual Hadoop cluster setup or management required.&nbsp; </p>\n<p><u><em>Built-in Information Production Monitoring and Dashboarding</em></u></p>\n<p>Data Factory also offers an up-to-the moment monitoring dashboard, which means you can deploy your data pipelines and immediately begin to view them as part of your monitoring dashboard.&nbsp; Once you have created and deployed pipelines to your Data Factory you can quickly assess end-to-end data pipeline health, pinpoint issues, and take corrective action as needed. </p>\n<p>Within the Azure Preview Portal, you get a visual layout of all of your pipelines and data inputs and outputs. You can see all the relationships and dependencies of your data pipelines across all of your sources so you always know where data is coming from and where it is going at a glance. We also provide you with a historical accounting of job execution, data production status, and system health in a single monitoring dashboard:</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/282efe892640_10ED0/image_26.png\"><img title=\"image\" style=\"border-left-width: 0px; border-right-width: 0px; border-bottom-width: 0px; display: inline; border-top-width: 0px\" border=\"0\" alt=\"image\" src=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/282efe892640_10ED0/image_thumb_12.png\" width=\"866\" height=\"444\"></a> </p>\n<p><u><em>Learning More about Stream Analytics Service</em></u></p>\n<p>For more information about Data Factory, please review the following resources:</p>\n<ul>\n<li><a href=\"http://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/documentation/articles/data-factory-get-started/\" target=\"_blank\">Getting Started Tutorial for Data Factory</a> \n<li><a href=\"http://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/documentation/services/data-factory\">More Data Factory Tutorials</a> \n<li><a href=\"http://go.microsoft.com/fwlink/?LinkId=516973\">Install the PowerShell SDK</a> \n<li><a href=\"http://go.microsoft.com/fwlink/?LinkId=516903\">Access our code sample repository</a></li></ul>\n<h2><u>Other Great Data Improvements</u></h2>\n<p>Today’s releases make it even easier for customers to stream, process and manage the movement of data in the cloud.&nbsp; Over the last few months we’ve released a bunch of other great data updates as well that make Azure a great platform to perform any data needs.&nbsp; Since August:&nbsp; <p>We released a major update of our <strong>SQL Database service</strong>, which is a relational database as a service offering.&nbsp; The <a href=\"http://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/services/sql-database/\" target=\"_blank\">new SQL DB editions</a> (Basic/Standard/Premium ) support a 99.99% SLA, larger database sizes, dedicated performance guarantees, point-in-time recovery, new auditing features, and the ability to easily setup active geo-DR support.&nbsp; </p>\n<p>We released a preview of our new <strong>DocumentDB service</strong>, which is a <a href=\"http://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/services/documentdb/\" target=\"_blank\">fully-managed, highly-scalable, NoSQL Document Database service</a> that supports saving and querying JSON based data.&nbsp; It enables you to linearly scale your document store and scale to any application size.&nbsp; <a href=\"http://azure.microsoft.com/blog/2014/10/09/azure-documentdb-profile-of-msn-health-and-fitness-2/\" target=\"_blank\">Microsoft MSN portal recently was rewritten to use it</a> – and stores more than 20TB of data within it.</p>\n<p>We released our new <strong>Redis Cache service</strong>, which is a <a href=\"http://weblogs.asp.net/scottgu/azure-redis-cache-disaster-recovery-to-azure-tagging-support-elastic-scale-for-sqldb-docdb\" target=\"_blank\">secure/dedicated Redis cache offering, managed as a service by Microsoft</a>.&nbsp; Redis is a popular open-source solution that enables high-performance data types, and our Redis Cache service enables you to standup an in-memory cache that can make the performance of any application much faster. </p>\n<p>We released major updates to our <strong>HDInsight Hadoop service</strong>, which is a 100% Apache Hadoop-based service in the cloud. We have also added built-in support for using two popular frameworks in the Hadoop ecosystem: <a href=\"http://azure.microsoft.com/blog/2014/08/25/azure-hdinsight-makes-hbase-nosql-database-a-ga-feature/\" target=\"_blank\">Apache HBase</a> and <a href=\"http://azure.microsoft.com/blog/2014/10/15/microsoft-brings-real-time-analytics-to-hadoop-with-storm-preview/\" target=\"_blank\">Apache Storm</a>. </p>\n<p>We released a preview of our new <strong>Search-As-A-Service offering</strong>, which provides a <a href=\"http://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/services/search/\" target=\"_blank\">managed search offering</a> based on ElasticSearch that you can easily integrate into any Web or Mobile Application.&nbsp; It enables you to build search experiences over any data your application uses (including data in SQLDB, DocDB, Hadoop and more). </p>\n<p>And we have released a preview of our <strong>Machine Learning service</strong>, which provides a <a href=\"http://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/services/machine-learning/\" target=\"_blank\">powerful cloud-based predictive analytics service</a>.&nbsp; It is designed for both new and experienced data scientists, includes 100s of algorithms from both the open source world and Microsoft Research, and supports writing ML solutions using the popular R open-source language.</p>\n<p>You’ll continue to see major data improvements in the months ahead – we have an exciting roadmap of improvements ahead.</p>\n<h4><u>Summary</u></h4>\n<p>Today’s Microsoft Azure release enables some great new data scenarios, and makes building applications that work with data in the cloud even easier. \n<p>If you don’t already have a Azure account, you can sign-up for a <a href=\"https://www.windowsazure.com/en-us/pricing/free-trial/\">free trial</a> and start using all of the above features today.&nbsp; Then visit the <a href=\"https://azure.com/\">Microsoft Azure Developer Center</a> to learn more about how to build apps with it. \n<p>Hope this helps, \n<p>Scott \n<p><em>P.S. 19:01:33","updatedTime":"2020-08-16 19:01:33","title":"Announcing Windows Server 2016 Containers Preview","link":"https://weblogs.asp.net:443/scottgu/announcing-windows-server-2016-containers-preview","description":"<p>At DockerCon this year, Mark Russinovich, CTO of Microsoft Azure, demonstrated the first ever application built using code running in both a Windows Server Container and a Linux container connected together. This demo helped demonstrate Microsoft's vision that in <a href=\"http://azure.microsoft.com/blog/2014/10/15/new-windows-server-containers-and-azure-support-for-docker/\">partnership</a> with Docker, we can help bring the Windows and Linux ecosystems together by enabling developers to build container-based distributed applications using the tools and platforms of their choice.  <p>Today we are excited to release the first preview of Windows Server Containers as part of our <a href=\"http://blogs.technet.com/b/server-cloud/archive/2015/08/19/new-windows-server-preview-fuels-application-innovation-with-containers-software-defined-datacenter-updates.aspx\" target=\"_blank\">Windows Server 2016 Technical Preview 3</a> release. We’re also announcing great updates from our close collaboration with Docker, including enabling support for the Windows platform in the Docker Engine and a preview of the Docker Engine for Windows. Our Visual Studio Tools for Docker, which we previewed earlier this year, have also been updated to support Windows Server Containers, providing you a seamless end-to-end experience straight from Visual Studio to develop and deploy code to both Windows Server and Linux containers. Last but not least, we’ve made it easy to get started with Windows Server Containers in Azure via a dedicated virtual machine image.  <h2><u>Windows Server Containers</u></h2> <p>Windows Server Containers create a highly agile Windows Server environment, enabling you to accelerate the DevOps process to efficiently build and deploy modern applications. With today’s preview release, millions of Windows developers will be able to experience the benefits of containers for the first time using the languages of their choice – whether .NET, ASP.NET, PowerShell or Python, Ruby on Rails, Java and many others. <p>Today’s announcement delivers on the promise we made in <a href=\"http://azure.microsoft.com/blog/2014/10/15/new-windows-server-containers-and-azure-support-for-docker/\">partnership</a> with Docker, the fast-growing open platform for distributed applications, to offer container and DevOps benefits to Linux and Windows Server users alike. Windows Server Containers are now part of the Docker open source project, and Microsoft is a founding member of the Open Container Initiative. Windows Server Containers can be deployed and managed either using the Docker client or PowerShell. <h2><u>Getting Started using Visual Studio</u></h2> <p>The preview of our <a href=\"http://aka.ms/vslovesdocker\" target=\"_blank\">Visual Studio Tools for Docker</a>, which enables developers to build and publish ASP.NET 5 Web Apps or console applications directly to a Docker container, has been updated to include support for today’s preview of Windows Server Containers. The extension automates creating and configuring your container host in Azure, building a container image which includes your application, and publishing it directly to your container host. You can download and install this extension, and read more about it, at the Visual Studio Gallery here: <a href=\"http://aka.ms/vslovesdocker\">http://aka.ms/vslovesdocker</a>.  <p>Once installed, developers can right-click on their projects within Visual Studio and select “Publish”: <p><a href=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/Windows-Live-Writer/d3b237e15f2b_12AFF/image_6.png\"><img title=\"image\" style=\"border-top: 0px; border-right: 0px; background-image: none; border-bottom: 0px; padding-top: 0px; padding-left: 0px; border-left: 0px; display: inline; padding-right: 0px\" border=\"0\" alt=\"image\" src=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/Windows-Live-Writer/d3b237e15f2b_12AFF/image_thumb_2.png\" width=\"672\" height=\"672\"></a> <p>Doing so will display a Publish dialog which will now include the ability to deploy to a Docker Container (on either a Windows Server or Linux machine): <p><a href=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/Windows-Live-Writer/d3b237e15f2b_12AFF/image_8.png\"><img title=\"image\" style=\"border-top: 0px; border-right: 0px; background-image: none; border-bottom: 0px; padding-top: 0px; padding-left: 0px; border-left: 0px; margin: 0px; display: inline; padding-right: 0px\" border=\"0\" alt=\"image\" src=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/Windows-Live-Writer/d3b237e15f2b_12AFF/image_thumb_3.png\" width=\"906\" height=\"712\"></a> <p>You can choose to deploy to any existing Docker host you already have running: <p><a href=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/Windows-Live-Writer/d3b237e15f2b_12AFF/image_10.png\"><img title=\"image\" style=\"border-top: 0px; border-right: 0px; background-image: none; border-bottom: 0px; padding-top: 0px; padding-left: 0px; border-left: 0px; margin: 0px; display: inline; padding-right: 0px\" border=\"0\" alt=\"image\" src=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/Windows-Live-Writer/d3b237e15f2b_12AFF/image_thumb_4.png\" width=\"791\" height=\"474\"></a> <p>Or use the dialog to create a new Virtual Machine running either Window Server or Linux with containers enabled.&nbsp; The below screen-shot shows how easy it is to create a new VM hosted on Azure that runs today’s Windows Server 2016 TP3 preview that supports Containers – you can do all of this (and deploy your apps to it) easily without ever having to leave the Visual Studio IDE: <p><a href=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/Windows-Live-Writer/d3b237e15f2b_12AFF/image_4.png\"><img title=\"image\" style=\"border-top: 0px; border-right: 0px; background-image: none; border-bottom: 0px; padding-top: 0px; padding-left: 0px; border-left: 0px; display: inline; padding-right: 0px\" border=\"0\" alt=\"image\" src=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/Windows-Live-Writer/d3b237e15f2b_12AFF/image_thumb_1.png\" width=\"843\" height=\"701\"></a>      <h2><u>Getting Started Using Azure</u></h2> <p>In June of last year, at the first DockerCon, we enabled a streamlined Azure experience for creating and managing Docker hosts in the cloud. Up until now these hosts have only run on Linux. With the new preview of Windows Server 2016 supporting Windows Server Containers, we have enabled a parallel experience for Windows users.  <p>Directly from the Azure Marketplace, users can now deploy a Windows Server 2016 virtual machine pre-configured with the container feature enabled and Docker Engine installed. Our quick start guide has all of the details including screen shots and a walkthrough video so take a look here <a href=\"https://msdn.microsoft.com/en-us/virtualization/windowscontainers/quick_start/azure_setup\">https://msdn.microsoft.com/en-us/virtualization/windowscontainers/quick_start/azure_setup</a>. <p><a href=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/Windows-Live-Writer/d3b237e15f2b_12AFF/image_14.png\"><img title=\"image\" style=\"border-top: 0px; border-right: 0px; background-image: none; border-bottom: 0px; padding-top: 0px; padding-left: 0px; border-left: 0px; margin: 0px; display: inline; padding-right: 0px\" border=\"0\" alt=\"image\" src=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/Windows-Live-Writer/d3b237e15f2b_12AFF/image_thumb_6.png\" width=\"916\" height=\"563\"></a> <p>Once your container host is up and running, the quick start guide includes step by step guides for creating and managing containers using both <a href=\"https://msdn.microsoft.com/en-us/virtualization/windowscontainers/quick_start/manage_docker\">Docker</a> and <a href=\"https://msdn.microsoft.com/en-us/virtualization/windowscontainers/quick_start/manage_powershell\">PowerShell</a>.  <h2><u>Getting Started Locally Using Hyper-V</u></h2> <p>Creating a virtual machine on your local machine using Hyper-V to act as your container host is now really easy. We’ve published some PowerShell scripts to GitHub that automate nearly the whole process so that you can get started experimenting with Windows Server Containers as quickly as possible. The quick start guide has all of the details at <a href=\"https://msdn.microsoft.com/en-us/virtualization/windowscontainers/quick_start/container_setup\">https://msdn.microsoft.com/en-us/virtualization/windowscontainers/quick_start/container_setup</a>. <p>Once your container host is up and running the quick start guide includes step by step guides for creating and managing containers using both <a href=\"https://msdn.microsoft.com/en-us/virtualization/windowscontainers/quick_start/manage_docker\">Docker</a> and <a href=\"https://msdn.microsoft.com/en-us/virtualization/windowscontainers/quick_start/manage_powershell\">PowerShell</a>.  <p><a href=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/Windows-Live-Writer/d3b237e15f2b_12AFF/image_12.png\"><img title=\"image\" style=\"border-top: 0px; border-right: 0px; background-image: none; border-bottom: 0px; padding-top: 0px; padding-left: 0px; border-left: 0px; margin: 0px; display: inline; padding-right: 0px\" border=\"0\" alt=\"image\" src=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/Windows-Live-Writer/d3b237e15f2b_12AFF/image_thumb_5.png\" width=\"877\" height=\"562\"></a> <h2><u>Additional Information and Resources</u></h2> <p>A great list of resources including links to past presentations on containers, blogs and samples can be found in the <a href=\"https://msdn.microsoft.com/virtualization/community/community_overview\">community</a> section of our documentation. We have also setup a dedicated <a href=\"https://social.msdn.microsoft.com/Forums/en-US/home?forum=windowscontainers\">Windows containers</a> forum where you can provide feedback, ask questions and report bugs. If you want to learn more about the technology behind containers I would highly recommend reading Mark Russinovich’s blog on “<a href=\"http://azure.microsoft.com/blog/2015/08/17/containers-docker-windows-and-trends/\">Containers: Docker, Windows and Trends</a>” that was published earlier this week. <h2><u>Summary</u></h2> <p>At the //Build conference earlier this year we talked about our plan to make containers a fundamental part of our application platform, and today’s releases are a set of significant steps in making this a reality.’ The decision we made to embrace Docker and the Docker ecosystem to enable this in both Azure and Windows Server has generated a lot of positive feedback and we are just getting started. <p>While there is still more work to be done, now users in the Window Server ecosystem can begin experiencing the world of containers. I highly recommend you download the Visual Studio Tools for Docker, create a Windows Container host in Azure or locally, and try out our PowerShell and Docker support. Edition","link":"https://weblogs.asp.net:443/scottgu/announcing-open-source-of-net-core-framework-net-core-distribution-for-linux-osx-and-free-visual-studio-community-edition","description":"<p>This week we are holding our <a href=\"http://www.visualstudio.com/connect-event-vs\">Connect() developer event</a> in New York City.&nbsp; This is an event that is being streamed online for free, and it covers some of the great new capabilities coming with the Visual Studio 2015 and .NET 5 releases.&nbsp; You can watch the event live as well as on-demand <a href=\"http://www.visualstudio.com/connect-event-vs\">here</a>.  <p>I just finished giving the opening keynote of the event during which I made several big announcements:</p> <h2><u>Announcing the Open Sourcing of the .NET Core Runtime and Libraries </u></h2> <p>Over the last several years we have integrated more and more open source technology into our .NET, Visual Studio, and Azure offerings.&nbsp; We have also begun to open source more of our own code and technology as well.</p> <p>Earlier this year, at the Build 2014 conference, I announced the creation of the <a href=\"http://www.dotnetfoundation.org/\" target=\"_blank\">.NET Foundation</a> – which is an independent organization designed to foster the development and collaboration of open source technologies for .NET.&nbsp; We have now open sourced ASP.NET, EF, Web API, NuGet and the \"Roslyn\" C# and VB compilers under it.&nbsp; </p> <p>It has been great to see the energy and innovation in these technologies since we made the open source announcements. We continue to have dedicated Microsoft teams working on each of them (several of the teams have more developers than ever before).&nbsp; The open source process is now enabling the teams to collaborate even more with other developers in the community, and <em>every single one</em> of the above projects have now accepted code contributions from developers outside Microsoft.&nbsp; The combination is enabling an even richer flow of ideas, and even better products.</p> <p><u><em>Open Sourcing the .NET Core Runtime and Libraries</em></u></p> <p>Today I’m excited to announce that we are going even further, and will be <strong>open sourcing the .NET Core Runtime</strong>.&nbsp; This will include everything needed to execute .NET code – including the CLR, Just-In-Time Compiler (JIT), Garbage Collector (GC), and core .NET base class libraries.</p> <p>We are releasing the source under the MIT open source license and are also issuing an explicit patent promise to clarify users patent rights to .NET.&nbsp; This morning, we published the public repository on GitHub where the project will be hosted: <a href=\"https://github.com/dotnet/corefx\" target=\"_blank\">https://github.com/dotnet/corefx</a>  <p>Today’s source release includes many of the newer core .NET framework libraries (ImmutableCollections, SIMD, XML and MetadataReader).&nbsp; These libraries are fully open, and are ready to accept contributions.&nbsp; Over the next several weeks and months we will continue to transfer source (including the Core CLR which is not there right now but in the process of being moved) into the repository and likewise make it open for contributions.  <p><u><em>What does this open sourcing mean?</em></u>  <p>Today’s open source announcement means that developers will have a fully supported, fully open source, fully cross platform .NET stack for creating server and cloud applications – including everything from the C#/VB compilers, to the CLR runtime, to the core .NET base class libraries, to the higher-level .NET Web, Data and API frameworks.  <p>It is an exciting day for .NET, and the new open source process will allow the .NET teams in Microsoft to collaborate even more deeply with other developers around the world.&nbsp; The result is going to be even better products for everyone.  <h2><u>Announcing .NET Core Framework on Linux and OSX</u></h2> <p>Last month at a Cloud Event we held in San Francisco, Satya Nadella – our CEO – showed a slide like this one where he talked about how Microsoft loves Linux:  <p><a href=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/fa5d1ce7201f_EFDE/image_4.png\"><img title=\"image\" style=\"border-left-width: 0px; border-right-width: 0px; border-bottom-width: 0px; display: inline; border-top-width: 0px\" border=\"0\" alt=\"image\" src=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/fa5d1ce7201f_EFDE/image_thumb_1.png\" width=\"560\" height=\"334\"></a>  <p>We’ve worked hard with <a href=\"http://azure.microsoft.com\" target=\"_blank\">Azure</a> to make it a first-class cloud platform for Linux based applications, and shared how more than 20% of all VMs running on Azure are Linux based.&nbsp; In fact, we now have 5 different Linux distributions officially supported for use on Azure – with full integration within our management portal and command-line extensibility.  <p><em><u>Bringing Core .NET to Linux and OS X</u></em>  <p>Today I’m excited to announce the .NET side of our Linux support.&nbsp; In addition to making the .NET server stack open-source, we are also going to release an official distribution of the .NET Core for Linux, as well as an official distribution of .NET Core for the Mac operation system as well.  <p>This will enable you to build .NET server and cloud applications and run them on both Windows Server and Linux.&nbsp; It is going to enable every developer – regardless of what operating system they use to develop or target – to use .NET. And to do so on a fully open source runtime.  <p>We will be working closely with the Mono community as we complete our Linux port.&nbsp; The Mono community have done a great job advancing .NET and Linux over the last decade.&nbsp; Releasing the .NET Core source under an open source license is going to enable us to collaborate together much more closely going forward.&nbsp; There are many Linux enhancements Mono has built that we would like to use, and likewise there are improvements Mono will be able to benefit from by being able to use the .NET source code.&nbsp; Today’s set of announcements are a big win for everyone.  <h2><u>Announcing Visual Studio Community Edition</u></h2> <p>I’m also excited to announce that we are launching a new <u>free edition </u>of Visual Studio today that will empower even more developers to build great apps and solutions.  <p>The new Visual Studio Community 2013 edition is a full-featured IDE.&nbsp; It supports multiple project types in one solution file in a single IDE, and has all of the productivity features and IDE extensibility capabilities (meaning you can use Xamarin, ReSharper, VsVim, and any other VSIX extension) that developers love in Visual Studio.  <p>It is now available <u>completely free</u> for:  <ul> <li>Any individual developer working on a commercial or non-commercial project  <li>Any developer contributing to an open source project  <li>Anyone in an academic research or course setting (e.g. students, teachers, classroom, online course)  <li>Any non-enterprise organization with 5 or fewer developers working on a commercial/non-commercial project together</li></ul> <p>We are making it available for download starting today, and developers can download and start using it immediately.&nbsp; There is no program you need to join to use it – simply visit <a href=\"http://www.visualstudio.com\" target=\"_blank\">www.visualstudio.com</a>, click the download button, and you are good to go.&nbsp; <p>It is going to enable even more developers to take advantage of Visual Studio and build even better applications.&nbsp; We are looking forward to seeing what you build with it.  <h2><u>Summary</u></h2> <p>It has never been a better time to be a software developer.&nbsp; Software is what enables organizations to succeed in today’s digital environment.&nbsp; It is what enables businesses to connect better with customers, to deliver amazing new experiences, to drive new revenue streams, and to run operations more efficiently.  <p>Using the cloud, every software developer on the planet can now create and build solutions that can reach millions of users, with no upfront costs, powered by a cloud infrastructure that delivers completely global reach.&nbsp; These apps need to work with any device, and to be able to consume and integrate with data anywhere.  <p>I'm excited to announce the release of our new Azure App Service today - which provides a powerful new offering to deliver these solutions.&nbsp; Azure App Service is an integrated service that enables you to create web and mobile apps for any platform or device, easily integrate with SaaS solutions (Office 365, Dynamics CRM, Salesforce, Twilio, etc), easily connect with on-premises applications (SAP, Oracle, Siebel, etc), and easily automate businesses processes while meeting stringent security, reliability, and scalability needs.  <h2><u>Azure App Service</u></h2> <p>Azure App Service includes the Web App + Mobile App capabilities that we previously delivered separately (as Azure Websites + Azure Mobile Services).&nbsp; It also includes powerful new Logic/Workflow App and API App capabilities that we are introducing today for the very first time - along with built-in connectors that make it super easy to build logic workflows that integrate with dozens of popular SaaS and on-premises applications (Office 365, SalesForce, Dynamics, OneDrive, Box, DropBox, Twilio, Twitter, Facebook, Marketo, and more).&nbsp; <p>All of these features can be used together at one low price.&nbsp; In fact, the new Azure App Service pricing is <u>exactly the same price as our previous Azure Websites offering</u>.&nbsp; If you are familiar with our Websites service you now get all of the features it previously supported, plus additional new mobile support, plus additional new workflow support, plus additional new connectors to dozens of SaaS and on-premises solutions <u>at no extra charge</u>.&nbsp; <p><strong><u>Web + Mobile + Logic + API Apps</u></strong>  <p>Azure App Service enables you to easily create Web + Mobile + Logic + API Apps:  <p><a href=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/AnnouncingthenewAzureAppService_122D1/image_4.png\"><img title=\"image\" style=\"border-left-width: 0px; border-right-width: 0px; border-bottom-width: 0px; display: inline; border-top-width: 0px\" border=\"0\" alt=\"image\" src=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/AnnouncingthenewAzureAppService_122D1/image_thumb_1.png\" width=\"828\" height=\"457\"></a>  <p>You can run any number of these app types within a single Azure App Service deployment.&nbsp; Your apps are automatically managed by Azure App Service and run in managed VMs isolated from other customers (meaning you don't have to worry about your app running in the same VM as another customer).&nbsp; You can use the built-in AutoScaling support within Azure App Service to automatically increase and decrease the number of VMs that your apps use based on the actual resource consumption of them.&nbsp; <p>This provides an incredibly cost-effective way to build and run highly scalable apps that provide both Web and Mobile experiences, and which contain automated business processes that integrate with a wide variety of apps and data sources.  <p>Below are additional details on the different app types supported by Azure App Service.&nbsp; Azure App Service is generally available starting today for Web apps, with the Mobile, Logic and API app types available in public preview:  <p><u><strong>Web Apps</strong></u>  <p>The Web App support within Azure App Service includes 100% of the capabilities previously supported by Azure Websites.&nbsp; This includes:  <ul> <li>Support for .NET, Node.js, Java, PHP, and Python code  <li>Built-in AutoScale support (automatically scale up/down based on real-world load)  <li>Integrated Visual Studio publishing as well as FTP publishing  <li>Continuous Integration/Deployment support with Visual Studio Online, GitHub, and BitBucket  <li>Virtual networking support and hybrid connections to on-premises networks and databases  <li>Staged deployment and test in production support  <li>WebJob support for long running background tasks</li></ul> <p>Customers who have previously deployed an app using the Azure Website service will notice today that they these apps are now called \"Web Apps\" within the Azure management portals.&nbsp; You can continue to run these apps exactly as before - or optionally now also add mobile + logic + API app support to your solution as well without having to pay anything more.  <p><u><strong>Mobile Apps</strong></u>  <p>The Mobile App support within Azure App Service provides the core capabilities we previously delivered using Azure Mobile Services.&nbsp; It also includes several new enhancements that we are introducing today including:  <ul> <li>Built-in AutoScale support (automatically scale up/down based on real-world load)  <li>Traffic Manager support (geographically scale your apps around the world)  <li>Continuous Integration/Deployment support with Visual Studio Online, GitHub, and BitBucket  <li>Virtual networking support and hybrid connections to on-premises databases  <li>Staged deployment and test in production support  <li>WebJob support for long running background tasks</li></ul> <p>Because we have an integrated App Service offering, you can now run both Web and Mobile Apps using a single Azure App Service deployment.&nbsp; This allows you to avoid having to pay for a separate web and mobile backend - and instead optionally pool your resources to save even more money.  <p><u><strong>Logic Apps</strong></u>  <p>The Logic App support within Azure App Services is brand new and enables you to automate workflows and business processes.&nbsp; For example, you could configure a workflow that automatically runs every time your app calls an API, or saves data within a database, or on a timer (e.g. once a minute) - and within your workflows you can do tasks like create/retrieve a record in Dynamics CRM or Salesforce, send an email or SMS message to a sales-rep to follow up on, post a message on Facebook or Twitter or Yammer, schedule a meeting/reminder in Office 365, etc.&nbsp; <p>Constructing such workflows is now super easy with Azure App Services.&nbsp; You can define a workflow either declaratively using a JSON file (which you can check-in as source code) or using the new Logic/Workflow designer introduced today within the Azure Portal.&nbsp; For example, below I've used the new Logic designer to configure an automatically recurring workflow that runs every minute, and which searches Twitter for tweets about Azure, and then automatically send SMS messages (using Twilio) to have employees follow-up on them:  <p><a href=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/AnnouncingthenewAzureAppService_122D1/image_14.png\"><img title=\"image\" style=\"border-left-width: 0px; border-right-width: 0px; border-bottom-width: 0px; display: inline; border-top-width: 0px\" border=\"0\" alt=\"image\" src=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/AnnouncingthenewAzureAppService_122D1/image_thumb_6.png\" width=\"900\" height=\"468\"></a>&nbsp; <p>Creating the above workflow is super easy and takes only a minute or so to do using the new Logic App designer.&nbsp; Once saved it will automatically run within the same VMs/Infrastructure that the Web Apps and Mobile Apps you've built using Azure App Service use as well.&nbsp; This means you don't have to deploy or pay for anything extra - if you deploy a Web or Mobile App on Azure you can now do all of the above workflow + integration scenarios <u>at no extra cost</u>.&nbsp; <p>Azure App Service today includes support for the following built-in connectors that you can use to construct and automate your Logic App workflows:  <p><a href=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/AnnouncingthenewAzureAppService_122D1/image_9.png\"><img title=\"image\" style=\"border-top: 0px; border-right: 0px; border-bottom: 0px; border-left: 0px; display: inline\" border=\"0\" alt=\"image\" src=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/AnnouncingthenewAzureAppService_122D1/image_thumb_2.png\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\"></a>  <p>Combined the above connectors provide a super powerful way to build and orchestrate tasks that run and scale within your apps.&nbsp; You can now build much richer web and mobile apps using it.  <p><a href=\"http://channel9.msdn.com/Shows/Azure-Friday/Azure-App-Service-Logic-Apps-with-Josh-Twist\" target=\"_blank\">Watch this Azure Friday video about Logic Apps</a> with Scott Hanselman and Josh Twist to learn more about how to use it.  <p><strong><u>API Apps</u></strong>  <p>The API Apps support within Azure App Service provides additional support that enables you to easily create, consume and call APIs - both APIs you create (using a framework like ASP.NET Web API or the equivalent in other languages) as well as APIs from other SaaS and cloud providers.  <p>API Apps enable simple access control and credential management within your applications, as well as automatic SDK generation support that enables you to easily expose and integrate APIs across a wide-variety of languages.&nbsp; You can optionally integrate these APIs with Logic Apps.  <h2><u>Getting Started</u></h2> <p>Getting started with Azure App Service is easy.&nbsp; Simply sign-into the <a href=\"http://portal.azure.com/\" target=\"_blank\">Azure Preview Portal</a> and click the \"New\" button in the bottom left of the screen.&nbsp; Select the \"Web + Mobile\" sub-menu and you can now create Web Apps, Mobile Apps, Logic Apps, and API Apps:  <p><a href=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/AnnouncingthenewAzureAppService_122D1/image_8.png\"><img title=\"image\" style=\"border-left-width: 0px; border-right-width: 0px; border-bottom-width: 0px; display: inline; border-top-width: 0px\" border=\"0\" alt=\"image\" src=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/AnnouncingthenewAzureAppService_122D1/image_thumb_3.png\" width=\"793\" height=\"793\"></a>&nbsp;</p> <p>You can create any number of Web, Mobile, Logic and API apps and run them on a single Azure App Service deployment at no additional cost.&nbsp;
