It is now available with an enterprise grade SLA and is available for everyone to use. <p>Microsoft Azure now offers two types of storage: Premium Storage and Standard Storage. Premium Storage stores data durably on Solid State Drives (SSDs) and provides high performance, low latency, disk storage with consistent performance delivery guarantees.</p> <p><a href=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/AnnouncingGeneralAvailabilityofAzurePrem_13B74/image_2.png\"><img title=\"image\" style=\"border-left-width: 0px; border-right-width: 0px; border-bottom-width: 0px; display: inline; border-top-width: 0px\" border=\"0\" alt=\"image\" src=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/AnnouncingGeneralAvailabilityofAzurePrem_13B74/image_thumb.png\" width=\"624\" height=\"352\" /></a> </p> <p>Premium Storage is ideal for I/O-sensitive workloads - and is especially great for database workloads hosted within Virtual Machines.&nbsp; You can optionally attach several premium storage disks to a single VM, and <strong>support</strong> <strong>up to 32 TB of disk storage per Virtual Machine and drive more than 64,000 IOPS per VM at less than 1 millisecond latency for read operations</strong>. This provides an incredibly fast storage option that enables you to run even more workloads in the cloud. <p>Using Premium Storage, Azure now offers the ability run more demanding applications - including high-volume SQL Server, Dynamics AX, Dynamics CRM, Exchange Server, MySQL, Oracle Database, IBM DB2, MongoDB, Cassandra, and SAP solutions. <h2><u>Durability</u></h2> <p>Durability of data is of utmost importance for any persistent storage option. Azure customers have critical applications that depend on the persistence of their data and high tolerance against failures. Premium Storage keeps three replicas of data within the same region, and ensures that a write operation will not be confirmed back until it has been durably replicated. This is a unique cloud capability provided only be Azure today. <p>In addition, you can also optionally create snapshots of your disks and copy those snapshots to a Standard GRS storage account - which enables you to maintain a geo-redundant snapshot of your data that is stored &gt; 400 miles away from your primary Azure region for disaster recovery purposes. <h2><u>Available Regions</u></h2> <p>Premium Storage is available today in the following Azure regions: \n      <ul> \n       <li>West US <li>East US 2 <li>West Europe <li>East China <li>Southeast Asia <li>West Japan</li></li></li></li></li></li>\n      </ul> <p>We will expand Premium Storage to run in all Azure regions in the near future. <h2><u>Getting Started</u></h2> <p>You can easily get started with Premium Storage starting today. Simply go to the Microsoft Azure Management Portal and create a new Premium Storage account. You can do this by creating a new Storage Account and selecting the “Premium Locally Redundant” storage option (note: this option is only listed if you select a region where Premium Storage is available). <p>Then create a new VM and select the “DS” series of VM sizes. The DS-series of VMs are optimized to work great with Premium Storage. When you create the DS VM you can simply point it at your Premium Storage account and you’ll be all set. <h2><u>Learning More</u></h2> <p>Learn more about Premium Storage from <a href=\"http://azure.microsoft.com/blog/2015/04/16/azure-premium-storage-now-generally-available-\" target=\"_blank\">Mark Russinovich's blog post on today's release</a>.&nbsp; You can also see a <a href=\"http://channel9.msdn.com/Blogs/Regular-IT-Guy/Azure-Premium-Storage-Demo\" target=\"_blank\">live 3 minute demo of Premium Storage</a> in action by watching <a href=\"http://channel9.msdn.com/Blogs/Regular-IT-Guy/Azure-Premium-Storage-Demo\" target=\"_blank\">Mark Russinovich’s video on premium storage</a>. In it Mark shows both a Windows Server and Linux VM driving more than 64,000 disk IOPS with low latency against a durable drive powered by Azure Premium Storage. <p><a href=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/AnnouncingGeneralAvailabilityofAzurePrem_13B74/image_4.png\"><img title=\"image\" style=\"border-left-width: 0px; border-right-width: 0px; border-bottom-width: 0px; display: inline; border-top-width: 0px\" border=\"0\" alt=\"image\" src=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/AnnouncingGeneralAvailabilityofAzurePrem_13B74/image_thumb_1.png\" width=\"624\" height=\"368\" /></a> </p> <p>You can also visit the following links for more information: \n           <ul> \n            <li><a href=\"http://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/services/storage/premium-storage/\" target=\"_blank\">Premium Storage overview</a> <li><a href=\"http://go.microsoft.com/fwlink/?LinkId=521969\">Premium Storage REST operations</a> <li><a href=\"http://go.microsoft.com/fwlink/?LinkId=521965\">\"DS\" series VM specifications</a> <li><a href=\"http://go.microsoft.com/fwlink/?LinkID=533289&amp;clcid=0x409\">Channel 9 video on Premium Storage</a></li></li></li></li>\n           </ul> <h2><u>Summary</u></h2> <p>We are very excited about the release of Azure Premium Storage. Premium Storage opens up so many new opportunities to use Azure to run workloads in the cloud – including migrating existing on-premises solutions. <p>As always, we would love to hear feedback via comments on this blog, the <a href=\"http://social.msdn.microsoft.com/Forums/windowsazure/en-US/home?forum=windowsazuredata\">Azure Storage MSDN forum</a> or send email to <a href=\"mailto:mastoragequestions@microsoft.com\">mastoragequestions@microsoft.com</a>. <p>Hope this helps, <p>Scott</p></p></p></p></p></p></p></p></p></p></p></p></p></p></p>","descriptionType":"text/html","publishedDate":"Thu, 16 Apr 2015 17:01:22 +0000","feedId":348,"bgimg":"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/AnnouncingGeneralAvailabilityofAzurePrem_13B74/image_thumb.png","linkMd5":"8f71631e66102d9d9017addd00b23c57","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn40@2020_5/2020/08/16/11-01-38-555_2945faa01a8d43e0.webp","destWidth":624,"destHeight":352,"author":"","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/AnnouncingGeneralAvailabilityofAzurePrem_13B74/image_thumb.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn88@2020_1/2020/08/16/11-01-42-615_2945faa01a8d43e0.webp","https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/AnnouncingGeneralAvailabilityofAzurePrem_13B74/image_thumb_1.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn92@2020_3/2020/08/16/11-01-41-892_459d70615e971180.webp"}},{"createdTime":"2020-08-16 19:01:33","updatedTime":"2020-08-16 19:01:33","title":"Azure: New Marketplace, Network Improvements, New Batch Service, Automation Service, more","link":"https://weblogs.asp.net:443/scottgu/azure-new-marketplace-network-improvements-new-batch-service-automation-service-more","description":"<p>Today we released a major set of updates to Microsoft Azure. Today’s updates include:</p> <ul> <li><strong>Marketplace</strong>: Announcing Azure Marketplace and partnerships with key technology partners  <li><strong>Networking</strong>: Network Security Groups, Multi-NIC, Forced Tunneling, Source IP Affinity, and much more  <li><strong>Batch Computing</strong>: Public Preview of the new Azure Batch Computing Service  <li><strong>Automation</strong>: General Availability of the Azure Automation Service <li><strong>Anti-malware</strong>: General Availability of Microsoft Anti-malware for Virtual Machines and Cloud Services  <li><strong>Virtual Machines</strong>: General Availability of many more VM extensions – PowerShell DSC, Octopus, VS Release Management </li></ul> <p>All of these improvements are now available to use immediately (note that some features are still in preview).&nbsp; Below are more details about them:  <h2><u>Marketplace: Announcing Azure Marketplace and partnerships with key technology partners</u></h2> <p>Last week, at our <a href=\"http://blogs.microsoft.com/blog/2014/10/20/delivering-complete-cloud-every-business-industry-geography/\" target=\"_blank\">Cloud Day event</a> in San Francisco, I announced a new Azure Marketplace that helps to better connect Azure customers with partners, ISVs and startups.&nbsp; With just a couple of clicks, you can now quickly discover, purchase, and deploy any number of solutions directly into Azure.  <p><u><em>Exploring the Marketplace</em></u>  <p>You can explore the Azure Marketplace by clicking the Marketplace title that is pinned by default to the home-screen of the Azure Preview Portal:  <p><a href=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/10eca7a7dba9_492A/image_26.png\"><img title=\"image\" style=\"border-left-width: 0px; border-right-width: 0px; border-bottom-width: 0px; display: inline; border-top-width: 0px\" border=\"0\" alt=\"image\" src=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/10eca7a7dba9_492A/image_thumb_12.png\" width=\"834\" height=\"513\"></a>  <p>Clicking the Marketplace tile will enable you to explore a large selection of applications, VM images, and services that you can provision into your Azure subscription:</p> <p><a href=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/10eca7a7dba9_492A/image_4.png\"><img title=\"image\" style=\"border-left-width: 0px; border-right-width: 0px; border-bottom-width: 0px; display: inline; border-top-width: 0px\" border=\"0\" alt=\"image\" src=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/10eca7a7dba9_492A/image_thumb_1.png\" width=\"879\" height=\"565\"></a> </p> <p>Using the marketplace provides a super easy way to take advantage of a rich ecosystem of applications and services integrated to run great with Azure.&nbsp; Today’s marketplace release includes multi-VM templates to run Hadoop clusters powered by Cloudera or Hortenworks, Linux VMs powered by Unbuntu, CoreOS, Suse, CentOS, Microsoft SharePoint Server Farms, Cassandra Clusters powered by DataStax, and a wide range of security virtual appliances.</p> <p>You can click any of the items in the gallery to learn more about them and optionally deploy them.&nbsp; Doing so will walk you though a simple to follow creation wizard that enables you to optionally configure how/where they will run, as well as display any additional pricing required for the apps/services/VM images that you select.</p> <p>For example, below is all it takes to stand-up an 8-node DataStax Enterprise cluster:</p> <p><a href=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/10eca7a7dba9_492A/image_28.png\"><img title=\"image\" style=\"border-top: 0px; border-right: 0px; border-bottom: 0px; border-left: 0px; display: inline\" border=\"0\" alt=\"image\" src=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/10eca7a7dba9_492A/image_thumb_13.png\" width=\"847\" height=\"800\"></a> </p> <p>Solutions you purchase through the Marketplace will be automatically billed to your Azure subscription (avoiding the need for you to setup a separate payment method).&nbsp; Virtual Machine images will support the ability to bring your own license or rent the image license by the hour (which is ideal for proof of concept solutions or cases where you need the solution for only a short period of time).&nbsp; Both Azure Direct customers as well as customers who pay using an Enterprise Agreement can take advantage of the Azure Marketplace starting today.</p> <p>You can <a href=\"http://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/marketplace/\" target=\"_blank\">learn more</a> about the Azure Marketplace as well as <a href=\"http://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/marketplace/\" target=\"_blank\">browse the items within it here</a>.</p> <h2><u>Networking: Lots and lots of New Features and Improvements</u></h2> <p>This week’s Azure update includes a ton of new capabilities to the Azure networking stack.&nbsp; You can use these new networking capabilities immediately in the North Europe region, and they will be supported worldwide in all regions in November 2014.&nbsp; The new network capabilities include:  <p><u><em>Network Security Groups</em></u>  <p>You can now create Network Security groups to define access control rules for inbound and outbound traffic to a Virtual machine or a group of virtual machines in a subnet. The security groups and the rules can be managed and updated independent of the life cycle of the VM.  <p><u><em>Multi-NIC Support</em></u></p> <p>You can now create and manage multiple virtual network interfaces (NICs) on a VM.&nbsp; Multi-NIC support is a fundamental requirement for a majority of network virtual appliances that can be deployed in Azure. Having this support now enabled within Azure will enable even richer network virtual appliances to be used.  <p><u><em>Forced Tunneling</em></u></p> <p>You can now redirect or “force” all Internet-bound traffic that originates in a cloud application back through an on-premises network via a Site-to-Site VPN tunnel for inspection and auditing. This is a critical security capability for enterprise grade applications.  <p><u><em>ExpressRoute Enhancements</em></u></p> <p>You can now share a single ExpressRoute connection across multiple Azure subscriptions. Additionally, a single Virtual Network in Azure can now be linked to more than one ExpressRoute circuit, thereby enabling much richer backup and disaster recovery scenarios.  <p><a href=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/10eca7a7dba9_492A/image_16.png\"><img title=\"image\" style=\"border-left-width: 0px; border-right-width: 0px; border-bottom-width: 0px; display: inline; border-top-width: 0px\" border=\"0\" alt=\"image\" src=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/10eca7a7dba9_492A/image_thumb_7.png\" width=\"374\" height=\"201\"></a>  <p><em><u>New VPN Gateway Sizes</u></em></p> <p>To cater to the growing hybrid connectivity throughput needs and the number of cross premise sites, we are announcing the availability of a higher performance Azure VPN gateway. This will enable a faster ExpressRoute and Site-to-Site VPN gateways with more tunnels.  <p><u><em>Operations and audit logs for VNet Gateways and ExpressRoute</em></u></p> <p>You can now view operations logs for Virtual Network Gateways and ExpressRoute circuits. The <a href=\"https://manage.windowsazure.com\">Azure portal</a> will now show operations logs and information on all API calls you make and important infrastructure changes made such as scheduled updates to gateways.  <p><em><u>Advanced Virtual Network Gateway policies</u></em></p> <p>We now enable the ability for you to control encryption for the tunnel between Virtual Networks. You now have a choice between 3DES, AES128, AES256 and Null encryption, and you can also enable Perfect Forward Secrecy (PFS) for IPsec/IKE gateways.  <p><em><u>Source IP Affinity</u></em></p> <p>The Azure Load Balancer now supports a new distribution mode called Source IP Affinity (also known as session affinity or client IP affinity). You can now load balance traffic based on a 2-tuple (Source-IP, Destination-IP) or 3-tuple (Source-IP, Destination-IP and Protocol) distribution modes.  <p><em><u>Nested policies for Traffic Manager</u></em></p> <p>You can now create nested policies for traffic management. This allows tremendous flexibility in creating powerful load-balancing and failover schemes to support the needs of larger, more complex deployments.</p> <p><u><em>Portal Support for Managing Internal Load Balancer, Reserved and Instance IP addresses for Virtual Machines</em></u></p> <p>It is now possible to use the Azure Preview Portal to manage creating and setting up internal load balancers, as well as reserved and instance IP addresses for virtual machines.</p> <h2><u>Automation: General Availability of Azure Automation Service</u></h2> <p>I am excited to announce the General Availability of the Azure Automation service. Azure Automation enables the creation, deployment, monitoring, and maintenance of resources in an Azure environment using a highly scalable and reliable workflow engine. The service can be used to orchestrate time-consuming and frequently repeated operational tasks across Azure and third-party systems while decreasing operating expenses.  <p>Azure Automation allows you to build runbooks (PowerShell Workflows) to describe your administration processes, provides a secure global assets store so you don’t need to hardcode sensitive information within your runbooks, and offers scheduling so that runbooks can be triggered automatically.</p> <p>Runbooks can automate a wide range of scenarios – from simple day to day manual tasks to complex processes that span multiple Azure services and 3rd party systems. Because Automation is built on PowerShell, you can take advantage of the many existing PowerShell modules, or author your own to integrate with third party systems.  <p><u><em>Creating and Editing Runbooks</em></u>  <p>You can create a runbook from scratch, or start by importing an existing template in the runbook gallery:  <p><a href=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/10eca7a7dba9_492A/image_8.png\"><img title=\"image\" style=\"border-left-width: 0px; border-right-width: 0px; border-bottom-width: 0px; display: inline; border-top-width: 0px\" border=\"0\" alt=\"image\" src=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/10eca7a7dba9_492A/image_thumb_3.png\" width=\"624\" height=\"409\"></a>  <p>Editing experience for runbooks can also be performed directly in the administration portal:  <p><a href=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/10eca7a7dba9_492A/image_10.png\"><img title=\"image\" style=\"border-left-width: 0px; border-right-width: 0px; border-bottom-width: 0px; display: inline; border-top-width: 0px\" border=\"0\" alt=\"image\" src=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/10eca7a7dba9_492A/image_thumb_4.png\" width=\"624\" height=\"473\"></a>  <p><u><em>Pricing</em></u>  <p>Available as a pay-as-you-go service, Automation is billed based on the number of job run time minutes used in a given Azure subscription.&nbsp; 500 minutes of free job runtime credits are also included each month for Azure customers to use at no charge.  <p><em><u>Learn More</u></em>  <p>To learn more about Azure Automation, check out the following resources:  <ul> <li><a href=\"http://azure.microsoft.com/blog/tag/azure-automation/\">Azure Automation Blogs</a>  <li><a href=\"http://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/services/automation/\">MSDN Documentation</a>  <li><a href=\"https://social.msdn.microsoft.com/Forums/en-US/home?forum=azureautomation\">Azure Automation Forum</a>  <li><a href=\"http://feedback.azure.com/forums/246290-azure-automation\">User Voice</a></li></ul> <h2><u>Batch Service: Preview of Azure Batch - new job scheduling service for parallel and HPC apps</u></h2> <p>I’m excited to announce the public preview of our new Azure Batch Service. This new platform service provides “job scheduling as a service” with auto-scaling of compute resources, making it easy to run large-scale parallel and high performance computing (HPC) work in Azure. You submit jobs, we start the VMs, run your tasks, handle any failures, and then shut things down as work completes.  <p>Azure Batch is the job scheduling engine that we use internally to manage encoding for Azure Media Services, and for testing Azure itself. With this preview, we are excited to expand our SDK with a new application framework from GreenButton, a company Microsoft acquired earlier in the year. The Azure Batch SDK makes it easy to cloud-enable parallel, cluster, and HPC applications by describing jobs with the required resources, data, and one or more compute tasks.  <p>Azure Batch can be used to run large volumes of similar tasks or applications in parallel, programmatically. A command line program or script takes a set of data files as input, processes the data in a series of tasks, and produces a set of output files. Examples of batch workloads that customers are running today in Azure include calculating risk for banks and insurance companies, designing new consumer and industrial products, sequencing genes and developing new drugs, searching for new energy sources, rendering 3D animations, and transcoding video.  <p>Azure Batch makes it easy for these customers to use hundreds, thousands, tens of thousands of cores, or more on demand. With job scheduling as a service, Azure developers can focus on using batch computing in their applications and delivering services without needing to build and manage a work queue, scaling resources up and down efficiently, dispatching tasks, and handling failures.  <p><a href=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/10eca7a7dba9_492A/image_24.png\"><img title=\"image\" style=\"border-left-width: 0px; border-right-width: 0px; border-bottom-width: 0px; display: inline; border-top-width: 0px\" border=\"0\" alt=\"image\" src=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/10eca7a7dba9_492A/image_thumb_11.png\" width=\"624\" height=\"351\"></a>  <p>The scale of Azure helps batch computing customers get their work done faster, experiment with different designs, run larger and more precise models, and test a large number of different scenarios without having to invest in and maintain large clusters.  <p><a href=\"http://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/services/batch/\" target=\"_blank\">Learn more</a> about Azure Batch and start using it for your applications today.  <h2><u>Virtual Machines: General Availability of Microsoft Anti-Malware for VMs and Cloud Services</u></h2> <p>I’m excited to announce that the Microsoft Anti-malware security extension for Virtual Machines and Cloud Services is now generally available.&nbsp; We are releasing it as a <u>free capability</u> that you can <u>use at no additional charge</u>.  <p>The Microsoft Anti-malware security extension can be used to help identify and remove viruses, spyware or other malicious software.&nbsp; It provides real-time protection from the latest threats and also supports on-demand scheduled scanning.&nbsp; Enabling it is a good security best practice for applications hosted either on-premises or in the cloud.  <p><u><em>Enabling the Anti-Malware Extension </em></u> <p>You can select and configure the Microsoft Antimalware security extension for virtual machines using the <a href=\"https://portal.azure.com/\">Azure preview portal</a>, Visual Studio or API’s/PowerShell.&nbsp; Antimalware events are then logged to the customer configured Azure Storage account via Azure Diagnostics and can be piped to HDInsight or a SIEM tool for further analysis. More information is available in the <a href=\"http://go.microsoft.com/fwlink/?linkid=398023&amp;clcid=0x409\">Microsoft Antimalware Whitepaper</a>.  <p>To enable antimalware feature on existing virtual machine, select the <b>EXTENSIONS</b> tile on a Virtual Machine in the Azure Preview Portal, then click <b>ADD</b> in the command bar and select the <b>Microsoft Antimalware </b>extension. Then, click <b>CREATE</b> and customize any settings:  <p><a href=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/10eca7a7dba9_492A/image_14.png\"><img title=\"image\" style=\"border-left-width: 0px; border-right-width: 0px; border-bottom-width: 0px; display: inline; border-top-width: 0px\" border=\"0\" alt=\"image\" src=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/10eca7a7dba9_492A/image_thumb_6.png\" width=\"918\" height=\"578\"></a>  <h2><u>Virtual Machines: General Availability of even more VM Extensions</u></h2> <p>In addition to enabling the Microsoft Anti-Malware extension for Virtual Machines, today’s release also includes support for a whole bunch more new VM extensions that you can enable within your Virtual Machines.&nbsp; These extensions can be added and configured using the same <strong>EXTENSIONS</strong> tile on Virtual Machine resources within the Azure Preview Portal (the same screen-shot as in the Anti-malware section above).</p> <p>The new extensions enabled today include:</p> <p><em><u>PowerShell Desired State Configuration</u></em></p> <p>The PowerShell Desired State Configuration Extension can be used to deploy and configure Azure VMs using <a href=\"http://technet.microsoft.com/en-us/library/dn249912.aspx\">Desired State Configuration</a> (DSC) technology. DSC enables you to declaratively specify how you want your software environment to be configured. DSC configuration can also be automated using the <a href=\"http://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/downloads/\">Azure PowerShell </a>SDK, and you can push configurations to any Azure VM and have them enacted automatically. For more details, please see this desired state configuration <a href=\"http://blogs.msdn.com/b/powershell/archive/2014/08/07/introducing-the-azure-powershell-dsc-desired-state-configuration-extension.aspx\">blog post</a>.  <p><a href=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/10eca7a7dba9_492A/image_20.png\"><img title=\"image\" style=\"border-left-width: 0px; border-right-width: 0px; border-bottom-width: 0px; display: inline; border-top-width: 0px\" border=\"0\" alt=\"image\" src=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/10eca7a7dba9_492A/image_thumb_9.png\" width=\"703\" height=\"415\"></a>&nbsp; <p><em><u>Octopus</u></em></p> <p><a href=\"http://octopusdeploy.com/\">Octopus</a> simplifies the deployment of <a href=\"http://ASP.NET\">ASP.NET</a> web applications, Windows Services and other applications by automatically configuring IIS, installing services and making configuration changes. Octopus integration of Azure was one of the top requested features on <a href=\"http://feedback.azure.com/forums/216843-virtual-machines/suggestions/5730576-add-octopus-deploy-agent-installation-option\">Azure UserVoice</a> and with this integration we will simplify the deployment and configuration of octopus on the VM.  <p><a href=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/10eca7a7dba9_492A/image_18.png\"><img title=\"image\" style=\"border-left-width: 0px; border-right-width: 0px; border-bottom-width: 0px; display: inline; border-top-width: 0px\" border=\"0\" alt=\"image\" src=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/10eca7a7dba9_492A/image_thumb_8.png\" width=\"692\" height=\"464\"></a> </p> <p><em><u>Visual Studio Release Management</u></em></p> <p>Release Management for Visual Studio is a continuous delivery solution that automates the release process through all of your environments from TFS through to production. Visual Studio Release Management is integrated with TFS and you can configure multi-stage release pipelines to automatically deploy and validate your applications on multiple environments. With the new Visual Studio Release Management extension, VMs can be preconfigured with the necessary components for required for Release Management to operate.  <p><a href=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/10eca7a7dba9_492A/image_22.png\"><img title=\"image\" style=\"border-left-width: 0px; border-right-width: 0px; border-bottom-width: 0px; display: inline; border-top-width: 0px\" border=\"0\" alt=\"image\" src=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/10eca7a7dba9_492A/image_thumb_10.png\" width=\"624\" height=\"393\"></a>  <h2><u>Summary</u></h2> <p>Today’s Microsoft Azure release enables a ton of great new scenarios, and makes building applications hosted in the cloud even easier.  <p>If you don’t already have a Azure account, you can sign-up for a <a href=\"https://www.windowsazure.com/en-us/pricing/free-trial/\" target=\"_blank\">free trial</a> and start using all of the above features today.&nbsp; Then visit the <a href=\"https://azure.com\" target=\"_blank\">Microsoft Azure Developer Center</a> to learn more about how to build apps with it.  <p>Hope this helps,  <p>Scott  <p><em>P.S. Azure GS-series of Virtual Machine sizes, which enable Azure Premium Storage to be used with Azure G-series VM sizes. These VM sizes are now available to use in both our US and Europe regions. <p><a href=\"http://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/blog/largest-vm-in-the-cloud/\" target=\"_blank\">Earlier this year</a> we released the G-series of Azure Virtual Machines – which provide the largest VM size provided by any public cloud provider.&nbsp; They provide up to <strong>32-cores of CPU, 448 GB of memory and 6.59 TB of local SSD-based storage</strong>.&nbsp; Today’s release of the GS-series of Azure Virtual Machines enables you to now use these large VMs with Azure Premium Storage – and enables you to perform up to <strong>2,000 MB/sec of storage throughput , more than double any other public cloud provider</strong>.&nbsp; Using the G5/GS5 VM size now also offers more than <strong>20 gbps of network bandwidth</strong>, also more than <strong>double the network throughout provided by any other public cloud provider</strong>.  <p>These new VM offerings provide an ideal solution to your most demanding cloud based workloads, and are great for relational databases like SQL Server, MySQL, PostGres and other large data warehouse solutions. You can also use the GS-series to significantly scale-up the performance of enterprise applications like Dynamics AX.  <p>The G and GS-series of VM sizes are available to use now in our West US, East US-2, and West Europe Azure regions.&nbsp; Simply navigate to the <a href=\"http://portal.azure.com/\">Azure Preview Portal</a>, select New(+) and choose your favorite OS or VM image type: <p><a href=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/Windows-Live-Writer/87c53b90a5cd_12FAD/image_2.png\"><img title=\"image\" style=\"border-top: 0px; border-right: 0px; background-image: none; border-bottom: 0px; padding-top: 0px; padding-left: 0px; border-left: 0px; display: inline; padding-right: 0px\" border=\"0\" alt=\"image\" src=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/Windows-Live-Writer/87c53b90a5cd_12FAD/image_thumb.png\" width=\"628\" height=\"358\"></a> <p>Click the Create button, and then click the pricing tier option and select “View All” to see the full list of VM sizes. Make sure your region is West US, East US 2, or West Europe to select the G-series or the GS-Series:</p> <p><a href=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/Windows-Live-Writer/87c53b90a5cd_12FAD/image_4.png\"><img title=\"image\" style=\"border-top: 0px; border-right: 0px; background-image: none; border-bottom: 0px; padding-top: 0px; padding-left: 0px; border-left: 0px; margin: 0px; display: inline; padding-right: 0px\" border=\"0\" alt=\"image\" src=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/Windows-Live-Writer/87c53b90a5cd_12FAD/image_thumb_1.png\" width=\"628\" height=\"466\"></a></p> <p>When choosing a GS-series VM size, the portal will create a storage account using Premium Azure Storage. You can select an existing Premium Storage account, as well, to use for the OS disk of the VM:  <p><a href=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/Windows-Live-Writer/87c53b90a5cd_12FAD/image_6.png\"><img title=\"image\" style=\"border-top: 0px; border-right: 0px; background-image: none; border-bottom: 0px; padding-top: 0px; padding-left: 0px; border-left: 0px; margin: 0px; display: inline; padding-right: 0px\" border=\"0\" alt=\"image\" src=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/Windows-Live-Writer/87c53b90a5cd_12FAD/image_thumb_2.png\" width=\"627\" height=\"312\"></a> <p>Hitting Create will launch and provision the VM.   <h2><u>Learn More</u></h2> <p>If you would like more information on the GS-Series VM sizes as well as other Azure VM Sizes then please visit the following page for additional details: <a href=\"https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/documentation/articles/virtual-machines-size-specs/\">Virtual Machine Sizes for Azure</a>.  <p>For more information on Premium Storage, please see: <a href=\"http://go.microsoft.com/fwlink/?LinkId=521898\">Premium Storage overview</a>. Also, refer to <a href=\"https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/documentation/articles/storage-premium-storage-preview-portal/#using-linux-vms-with-premium-storage\">Using Linux VMs with Premium Storage</a> for more details on Linux deployments on Premium Storage.  <p>Hope this helps, <p>Scott</p>","descriptionType":"text/html","publishedDate":"Wed, 02 Sep 2015 17:51:22 +0000","feedId":348,"bgimg":"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/Windows-Live-Writer/87c53b90a5cd_12FAD/image_thumb.png","linkMd5":"90da1a52d03a08afb9551b6d259ded90","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn87@2020_3/2020/08/16/11-01-39-301_d9d3e92aa73dee3e.webp","destWidth":628,"destHeight":358,"author":"","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/Windows-Live-Writer/87c53b90a5cd_12FAD/image_thumb.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn83@2020_4/2020/08/16/11-01-41-311_d9d3e92aa73dee3e.webp","https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/Windows-Live-Writer/87c53b90a5cd_12FAD/image_thumb_1.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx17/cdn51@2020_6/2020/08/16/11-01-39-849_b71f0e007ee1df12.webp","https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/Windows-Live-Writer/87c53b90a5cd_12FAD/image_thumb_2.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn84@2020_5/2020/08/16/11-01-40-559_24a2b20c979901ed.webp"}},{"createdTime":"2020-08-16 19:01:33","updatedTime":"2020-08-16 19:01:33","title":"Azure: Premium Storage, RemoteApp, SQL Database Update, Live Media Streaming, Search and More","link":"https://weblogs.asp.net:443/scottgu/azure-premium-storage-remoteapp-sql-database-update-live-media-streaming-search-and-more","description":"<p>Today we released a number of great enhancements to Microsoft Azure. These include:</p> <ul> <li><strong>Premium Storage</strong>: New Premium high-performance Storage for Azure Virtual Machine workloads  <li><strong>RemoteApp</strong>: General Availability of Azure RemoteApp service  <li><strong>SQL Database</strong>: Enhancements to Azure SQL Databases  <li><strong>Media Services</strong>: General Availability of Live Channels for Media Streaming  <li><strong>Azure Search</strong>: Enhanced management experience, multi-language support and more  <li><strong>DocumentDB</strong>: Support for Bulk Add Documents and Query Syntax Highlighting  <li><strong>Site Recovery</strong>: General Availability of disaster recovery to Azure for branch offices and SMB customers  <li><strong>Azure Active Directory</strong>: General Availability of Azure Active Directory application proxy and password write back support </li></ul> <p>All of these improvements are now available to use immediately (note that some features are still in preview).&nbsp; Below are more details about them:  <h2><u>Premium Storage: High-performance Storage for Virtual Machines</u></h2> <p>I’m excited to announce the public preview of our new Azure Premium Storage offering. With the introduction of the new Premium Storage option, Azure now offers two types of durable storage: Premium Storage and Standard Storage. Premium Storage stores data durably on Solid State Drives (SSDs) and provides high performance, low latency, disk storage with consistent performance delivery guarantees.  <p><a href=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/a2f3e6cdd02d_1280A/image_20.png\"><img title=\"image\" style=\"border-left-width: 0px; border-right-width: 0px; border-bottom-width: 0px; display: inline; border-top-width: 0px\" border=\"0\" alt=\"image\" src=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/a2f3e6cdd02d_1280A/image_thumb_9.png\" width=\"640\" height=\"360\"></a>  <p>Premium Storage is ideal for I/O-sensitive workloads - and is great for database workloads hosted within Virtual Machines.&nbsp; You can optionally attach several premium storage disks to a single VM, and <strong>support</strong> <strong>up to 32 TB of disk storage per Virtual Machine and drive more than 50,000 IOPS per VM at less than 1 millisecond latency for read operations</strong>. This provides a wickedly fast storage option that enables you to run even more workloads in the cloud. </p> <p>Using Premium Storage, Azure now offers the ability to \"lift-and-shift\" more demanding enterprise applications to the cloud - including SQL Server, Dynamics AX, Dynamics CRM, Exchange Server, MySQL, Oracle Database, IBM DB2, and SAP Business Suite solutions.</p> <p>Premium Storage is now available in public preview starting today. To sign up to use the Azure Premium Storage preview, visit the <a href=\"http://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/services/preview/\">Azure Preview page</a>.  <h4><em><u>Disk Sizes and Performance</u></em></h4> <p>Premium Storage disks provide up to 5,000 IOPS and 200 MB/sec throughput depending on the disk size. When you create a new premium storage disk you get the option to select the disk size and performance characteristics you want based on your application performance and storage capacity needs.&nbsp; For the public preview, we are offering three Premium Storage disk configurations:</p> <table class=\"GridTable7Colorful1\" style=\"border-top: medium none; To learn the disk bandwidth available for each VM size, see the <a href=\"http://msdn.microsoft.com/en-us/library/azure/dn197896.aspx\">Virtual Machine and Cloud Service Sizes for Azure</a>  <h4><em><u>Durability</u></em></h4> <p>Durability of data is of utmost importance for any persistent storage option. Azure customers have critical applications that depend on the persistence of their data and high tolerance against failures. Premium Storage keeps three replicas of data within the same region. In addition, you can also optionally create snapshots of your disks and copy those snapshots to a Standard GRS storage account - which enables you to maintain a geo-redundant snapshot of your data that is stored at least 400 miles away from your primary Azure region.  <h4><u><em>Learn More</em> </u></h4> <p>You can learn more about Premium Storage disks <a href=\"http://go.microsoft.com/fwlink/?LinkId=521898\">here</a>.&nbsp; To sign up to use Premium Storage, go to the <a href=\"http://www.windowsazure.com/en-us/services/preview/\">Azure Preview</a> page, and sign up for Microsoft Azure Premium Storage service using your subscription.  <h2><u>RemoteApp: General Availability of Azure RemoteApp</u></h2> <p>I’m excited to announce the general availability of Azure RemoteApp. Using Azure RemoteApp, you can deploy Windows desktop applications in the cloud, and provide your users with an intuitive, high-fidelity, WAN-ready remote application experience.&nbsp; Users can use the cloud-hosted Windows applications you enable on their phones, tablets, or PCs - <strong>including Windows, Mac, iOS and Android based devices</strong>.&nbsp; We are delivering RemoteApp with a <strong>super competitive price</strong> - you can host your user's applications in the cloud for just <strong>$10/user/month</strong>.&nbsp; With today’s release, Azure RemoteApp is backed by an <a href=\"http://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/support/legal/sla/\">SLA</a> and supported by Microsoft Support, offering the full scalability and security of the Azure cloud.  <h4><em><u>Getting Started</u></em></h4> <p>Setting up RemoteApp is easy. In the <a href=\"https://manage.windowsazure.com\">Azure Management Portal</a>, select <b>NEW -&gt; App Services -&gt; RemoteApp -&gt; Quick Create. </b>Pick a name, region, select the scale configuration plan you want to use, pick one of the standard template images, and click OK. When you do this for the first time, your 30-day free trial will also start. This is a fully featured trial, available to all Azure customers.  <p><a href=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/a2f3e6cdd02d_1280A/image_4.png\"><img title=\"image\" style=\"border-left-width: 0px; border-right-width: 0px; border-bottom-width: 0px; display: inline; border-top-width: 0px\" border=\"0\" alt=\"image\" src=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/a2f3e6cdd02d_1280A/image_thumb_1.png\" width=\"768\" height=\"480\"></a>  <p>A RemoteApp instance is an elastic, automatically scaled, collection of Windows Server VMs that are running the Remote Desktop Session Host role and host the applications. The VMs are all created based on the template image you provide. You can provide your own template image containing your custom apps, or use one of the standard template images we provide. One of these is for Office 365 ProPlus, which you can use if you have a subscription that contains the Office 365 ProPlus service:  <p><a href=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/a2f3e6cdd02d_1280A/image_6.png\"><img title=\"image\" style=\"border-left-width: 0px; border-right-width: 0px; border-bottom-width: 0px; display: inline; border-top-width: 0px\" border=\"0\" alt=\"image\" src=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/a2f3e6cdd02d_1280A/image_thumb_2.png\" width=\"768\" height=\"480\"></a>  <p>Once enabled, your users can quickly and easily connect to the applications you host in Azure.&nbsp; They can use Windows, Mac, iOS and Android devices to connect to the RemoteApp service - enabling you to use Azure to run your Windows desktop applications anywhere in the world, on any device.  <h4><em><u>Enabling Hybrid Applications</u></em></h4> <p>Many business-critical Windows applications rely on on-premises infrastructure such as identity and machine management, and require access to on-premises databases and resources. Azure RemoteApp provides a hybrid deployment model that supports all of these scenarios.  <ul> <li> <p><b>Hybrid Management</b>: In a hybrid RemoteApp collection, the VMs which host your applications are joined to your AD domain. Therefore, you can use on-premises management tools like Group Policy, System Center, and many other enterprise management tools that rely on AD membership. </p></li></ul> <ul> <li><b>Federated Identity</b>: You can use Azure Active Directory integrated with your on-premises AD and your users can logon with their familiar corporate identities. When the Windows applications starts, it is running in a fully domain-joined session, with the usual integrated authentication capabilities of a Windows domain. </li></ul> <ul> <li> <p><strong>Hybrid Networking</strong>: Windows applications in a hybrid RemoteApp collection can seamlessly access on-premises data and resources. This capability is built on Azure Virtual Networking with site-to-site VPN, providing cloud-premise virtual network connectivity. In the future, RemoteApp collections will support full range of Azure Networking capabilities, including ExpressRoute. </p></li></ul> <h4><em><u>Performance and Scale Configurations</u></em></h4> <p>With today's general availability release, we are offering two scale configurations: <b>BASIC </b>and<b> STANDARD</b>.  <ul> <li>BASIC is intended for lighter, task-worker use cases, such as a single productivity application or a data-entry frontend to a line of business system. </li></ul> <ul> <li>STANDARD is intended for typical productivity use cases such as using Outlook, Word, Excel and other knowledge worker line of business and productivity applications. </li></ul> <p>You can select the scale configuration for your RemoteApp collection while creating it. If you want to change it later, you can do so using the <b>SCALE</b> tab. Your applications and settings and your user data remain intact through this change.  <p><a href=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/a2f3e6cdd02d_1280A/image_8.png\"><img title=\"image\" style=\"border-left-width: 0px; border-right-width: 0px; border-bottom-width: 0px; display: inline; border-top-width: 0px\" border=\"0\" alt=\"image\" src=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/a2f3e6cdd02d_1280A/image_thumb_3.png\" width=\"768\" height=\"480\"></a>  <h4><em><u>Pricing</u></em></h4> <p>We are making the RemoteApp service available at a very attractive, affordable price.&nbsp; You can host a <b>line of business Windows application for as little as $10/user per month</b> using the BASIC configuration.  <p>At the STANDARD level, you can host your users’ <b>entire productivity workspace for just $15/user per month</b>.  <p></p> <h4><em><u>Learn More</u></em></h4> <p>A variety of resources are available on the <a href=\"http://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/services/remoteapp/\">RemoteApp overview page</a>. You can also <a href=\"http://remoteapp.azure.com/\">download the client for your device</a> and take a test drive. Finally, <a href=\"http://blogs.msdn.com/b/rds/archive/2014/12/11/windows-apps-in-the-cloud-azure-remoteapp-now-generally-available.aspx\">RDV Team blog</a> discusses today’s new features in more detail.  <h2><u>SQL Databases: Now with SQL 2014 Features and Compatibility</u></h2> <p>Today we are making available a preview of the next-generation release of our Azure SQL Database service.&nbsp; We announced some of the preview's new features <a href=\"http://azure.microsoft.com/blog/2014/11/05/preview-for-greater-sql-server-compatibility-coming-soon-to-azure-sql-database/\">earlier in November</a>.&nbsp; Today's release delivers near-complete SQL Server 2014 engine compatibility and even better performance.  <p>Our internal benchmark tests (using over 600 million rows of data) show query performance improvements of around 5x with today's preview relative to our existing Premium Tier SQL Database offering and up to 100x performance improvements when using the new In-memory columnstore technology now supported with today's preview release.  <h4><em><u>Lots of great new features and improvements</u></em></h4> <p>Key highlights of today's preview include:  <ul> <li> <p><strong>Better management of large databases. </strong>We now support heavier database workload management with parallel queries<i>,</i> table partitioning, online indexing, worry-free large index rebuilds with the previous 2GB size limit removed, and<em> </em>more<em> </em>alter database commands. </p></li></ul> <ul> <li> <p><strong>Support for more programmability capabilities: </strong>You can now build even more robust applications with CLR, T-SQL Windows functions, XML index, and change tracking support. </p></li></ul> <ul> <li> <p><b>Up to 100x performance improvements </b>with support for In-memory columnstore queries for data mart and analytic workloads. </p></li></ul> <ul> <li> <p><b>Improved monitoring and troubleshooting:</b> Extended Events (XEvents) and visibility into over 100 new table views via an expanded set of Database Management Views (DMVs). </p></li></ul> <ul> <li> <p><strong>New S3 performance level: </strong>Today's preview introduces a new pricing option for SQL Databases. The new \"S3\" performance tier delivers 100 DTU of performance (twice the DTU level of the existing S2 tier) and all of the features available in the Standard tier. It enables an even more cost effective way to run applications with higher performance needs. </p></li></ul> <h4><em><u>Learn More and Get Started</u></em></h4> <p>You can read more about the enhancements in today's preview on the <a href=\"http://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/documentation/articles/sql-database-preview-whats-new/\">preview getting started page</a>.&nbsp; To use today's preview, you can navigate to the <b>SETTINGS</b> part on the SQL Database blade in the <a href=\"https://portal.azure.com/\">Azure Preview Portal</a> and upgrade to use the preview.</p> <p><a href=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/a2f3e6cdd02d_1280A/image_10.png\"><img title=\"image\" style=\"border-left-width: 0px; border-right-width: 0px; border-bottom-width: 0px; display: inline; border-top-width: 0px\" border=\"0\" alt=\"image\" src=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/a2f3e6cdd02d_1280A/image_thumb_4.png\" width=\"624\" height=\"348\"></a>  <p>Try our the new features and give us your feedback!  <h2><u>Media Services: General Availability of Live Media Streaming</u></h2> <p>I’m very excited to announce the General Availability of Live Channels<b> </b>Media Streaming support.&nbsp; Live Channels with Azure Media Services is the live services backbone that broadcasters such as <strong>NBC Sports</strong> have used to deliver live online media streamed events such as <strong>English Premier League</strong>, <strong>NHL hockey</strong>, <strong>Sunday Night Football.&nbsp; </strong>A dozen international broadcasters also used it to seamlessly deliver live media streaming coverage of the <strong>2014 Sochi Winter Olympics</strong> and <strong>2014 FIFA World Cup</strong>.  <p>You can now use Live Channels to stream events of your own - and scale to literally millions of users watching them.&nbsp; Today's general availability release is backed by an enterprise-grade Service-Level Agreement (SLA)<b> </b>for all customers.&nbsp; <p><img title=\"Live Streaming\" alt=\"Live Streaming\" src=\"http://i.msdn.microsoft.com/dynimg/IC759890.png\"> <h4><em><u>Learn More</u></em></h4> <p>For more information on functionality and pricing, visit the <a href=\"http://azure.microsoft.com/blog/2014/09/10/getting-started-with-live-streaming-using-the-azure-management-portal/\">Getting Started with Live Streaming</a> blog post, the <a href=\"http://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/services/media-services/\">Media Services</a> webpage or <a href=\"http://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/pricing/details/media-services/\">Media Services Pricing</a> webpage, or the <a href=\"http://msdn.microsoft.com/en-us/library/dn783466.aspx\">Live Streaming</a> MSDN section.</p> <h2><u>Search: Portal Management, Multi-language support</u></h2> <p>I am happy to announce a number of highly requested features available today in <a href=\"http://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/services/search/\" target=\"_blank\">Azure Search</a>.&nbsp; Azure Search provides developers with all of the features needed to build out search experience for web and mobile applications without having to deal with the typical complexities that come with managing, tuning and scaling a real-world search service.&nbsp; <h4><em><u>Azure Portal Enhancements </u></em></h4> <p>Helping developers setup and manage their services quickly and easily is a key goal of the <a href=\"https://portal.azure.com/\">Azure Management Portal</a>. Today's release adds several new capabilities to the Azure Search support in the portal that makes it even easier to get started with Azure Search and reduce the need to write code.  <p>For example, you can now easily create a new index. In the portal, you can name the search index, set all of the fields, and assign the properties for each of them - all without writing any code:  <p><a href=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/a2f3e6cdd02d_1280A/image_12.png\"><img title=\"image\" style=\"border-left-width: 0px; border-right-width: 0px; border-bottom-width: 0px; display: inline; border-top-width: 0px\" border=\"0\" alt=\"image\" src=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/a2f3e6cdd02d_1280A/image_thumb_5.png\" width=\"624\" height=\"317\"></a> </p> <p>Once you create the index, you can also now drill into usage details like document counts and storage size. You can see all of the fields associated with this index as shown below:  <p><a href=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/a2f3e6cdd02d_1280A/image_14.png\"><img title=\"image\" style=\"border-left-width: 0px; border-right-width: 0px; border-bottom-width: 0px; display: inline; border-top-width: 0px\" border=\"0\" alt=\"image\" src=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/a2f3e6cdd02d_1280A/image_thumb_6.png\" width=\"429\" height=\"595\"></a> </p> <p>Index tuning is another enhancement now supported in the portal user interface. Boosting relevant items not only provides a better search experience, it also helps you achieve business objectives. For example, if you are searching a product index, you might want to boost documents where the result was found in the product name, as opposed to another document where the result was found in the product description. Or you may wish to use a scoring function that allows you to boost items that have high star ratings or that provide higher margins.  <p>The task of tuning an index was previously only available through the API. Starting today, using the <a href=\"https://portal.azure.com/\">Azure Preview portal</a> you can create or alter <a href=\"http://msdn.microsoft.com/en-us/library/azure/dn798928.aspx\">scoring profiles</a>, instantly tuning the results of your search queries without having to write a line of code:  <p><a href=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/a2f3e6cdd02d_1280A/image_16.png\"><img title=\"image\" style=\"border-left-width: 0px; border-right-width: 0px; border-bottom-width: 0px; display: inline; border-top-width: 0px\" border=\"0\" alt=\"image\" src=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/a2f3e6cdd02d_1280A/image_thumb_7.png\" width=\"589\" height=\"459\"></a>  <h4><em><u>Multilanguage Support across 27 Languages</u></em></h4> <p></p> <p></p> <p>With today’s release, Azure Search now has support for <a href=\"http://msdn.microsoft.com/en-us/library/azure/dn879793.aspx\">27 languages</a>. This allows Azure Search to accommodate the unique characteristics of a given language, enabling word-breaking and text normalization to work as expected for each language. Part of this enhancement includes support for stemming in the relevant languages, reducing words to their <a href=\"http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stemming\">word stems</a>. For example, you can search for the word “runs” and find documents that say “run” or “running”.  <p>When creating an index you can choose to include content from multiple languages, allowing you to search and return results based on the chosen language of your user. For more information, you can visit the <a href=\"http://msdn.microsoft.com/en-us/library/azure/dn879793.aspx\">Language Support page</a>. Over time, we will continue to enhance multi-language support to include additional languages.  <h4><em><u>API features</u></em></h4> <p>Last but not least, we’ve introduced a new <a href=\"http://msdn.microsoft.com/en-us/library/azure/dn832684.aspx\">Azure Search Management REST API</a> that allows you to perform common administrative tasks, such as creating new services, and scaling services to allow for additional storage or higher query-per-second rates. You can see a sample of how to use this <a href=\"https://azuresearchmgmtapi.codeplex.com/\">Management API at CodePlex</a>.  <h2><u>Document DB: Bulk Add Documents and Syntax Highlighting</u></h2> <p><a href=\"http://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/services/documentdb/\" target=\"_blank\">DocumentDB</a> is a NoSQL document database service designed for scalable and high performance modern applications.&nbsp; DocumentDB is delivered as a fully managed service (meaning you don’t have to manage any infrastructure or VMs yourself) with an enterprise grade SLA.  <p>We now support some nice new capabilities for Document DB in the <a href=\"https://portal.azure.com/\">Azure Preview Portal</a>:  <ul> <li><strong>Add Documents: </strong>Upload existing JSON documents via Document Explorer  <li><strong>Query syntax highlighting: </strong>Document DB SQL query </li></ul> <p>These features make it even easier to get started and explore DocumentDB.</p> <h4><em>Add Documents Support within the Azure Portal</em></h4> <p>The DocumentDB Document Explorer within the Azure Preview Portal now supports the uploading of existing JSON documents - which makes it easy to import and start using existing data stored in existing JSON files. Simply open Document Explorer and click the <b>Add Document </b>command:  <p><a href=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/a2f3e6cdd02d_1280A/image_22.png\"><img title=\"image\" style=\"border-left-width: 0px; border-right-width: 0px; border-bottom-width: 0px; display: inline; border-top-width: 0px\" border=\"0\" alt=\"image\" src=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/a2f3e6cdd02d_1280A/image_thumb_10.png\" width=\"313\" height=\"401\"></a>  <p>In the new blade that opens, click the browse button to open a file explorer and select 1 or more JSON documents to upload. Note that Document Explorer currently supports up to 100 JSON document files in a single upload operation.  <p><a href=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/a2f3e6cdd02d_1280A/image_24.png\"><img title=\"image\" style=\"border-left-width: 0px; border-right-width: 0px; border-bottom-width: 0px; display: inline; border-top-width: 0px\" border=\"0\" alt=\"image\" src=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/a2f3e6cdd02d_1280A/image_thumb_11.png\" width=\"624\" height=\"280\"></a>  <p>Once you’re satisfied with your selection, click the <b>upload</b> button. The documents will automatically be added to the Document Explorer grid and aggregate results will be displayed as the upload operation is in progress.  <p><a href=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/a2f3e6cdd02d_1280A/image_26.png\"><img title=\"image\" style=\"border-left-width: 0px; border-right-width: 0px; border-bottom-width: 0px; display: inline; border-top-width: 0px\" border=\"0\" alt=\"image\" src=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/a2f3e6cdd02d_1280A/image_thumb_12.png\" width=\"624\" height=\"396\"></a>  <p>Once the operation has completed, you can select up to another 100 documents to upload without having to close the Add Document blade.&nbsp; This makes it easy to import data into your DocumentDB databases.  <h4><em><u>Query Explorer – Syntax Highlighting</u></em></h4> <p>We’ve also enabled basic keyword and value highlighting within Query Explorer.  <p><a href=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/a2f3e6cdd02d_1280A/image_28.png\"><img title=\"image\" style=\"border-left-width: 0px; border-right-width: 0px; border-bottom-width: 0px; display: inline; border-top-width: 0px\" border=\"0\" alt=\"image\" src=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/a2f3e6cdd02d_1280A/image_thumb_13.png\" width=\"486\" height=\"358\"></a>  <p>This makes it even easier to experiment and test queries against your NoSQL databases.  <p>Please send us your feedback and suggestions on the Microsoft Azure DocumentDB <a href=\"http://feedback.azure.com/forums/263030-documentdb?filter=top&amp;page=1\">feedback forum</a>. If you haven’t tried DocumentDB yet, you can learn more about how to get started <a href=\"http://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/services/documentdb/\">here</a>.  <h2><u>Disaster Recovery: GA of DR for Branch Offices &amp; SMB Customers</u></h2> <p>I’m excited to announce the General Availability of the <b>Disaster Recovery (DR) to Azure for Branch offices and SMB feature </b>in our Azure Site Recovery (ASR) service.&nbsp; Today's new support enables consistent replication, protection, and recovery of Virtual Machines directly in Microsoft Azure.&nbsp; With this new support we have extended the Azure Site Recovery service to become a simple, reliable &amp; cost effective DR Solution for enabling Virtual Machine replication and recovery between Windows Server 2012 R2 and Microsoft Azure without having to deploy a System Center Virtual Machine Manager on your primary site.  <p>These features<b> </b>builds on top of the Hyper-V Replica technology available in Windows Server 2012 R2 and Microsoft Azure to provide remote health monitoring, no-impact recovery plan testing and single click orchestrated recovery – all of this backed by an SLA that is enterprise grade.  <h4><em><u>Verify DR Plans with Confidence</u></em></h4> <p>The <b>Test Failover</b> feature within Azure Site Recovery allows you to test your disaster recovery plans <u>without impacting your production workload</u> which ensures that you can perform periodic DR drills to meet your compliance objectives. You can connect to the virtual machine running in Azure via RDP after enabling the appropriate endpoints for the virtual machine running in Azure.  <p>A <b>Planned Failover</b> will do a shutdown of your on-premises machine, transfer all the last changes inside the virtual machine to Azure &amp; then bring up an instance of the VM in Azure without any data loss. An <b>Unplanned Failover</b> is usually triggered when your on-premises site has been hit by an unexpected disaster.  <p>If you are looking for failing over a multi-virtual machine application, you can do so using the <a href=\"http://aka.ms/asr_ga_blog_rp_blog\">One-Click Orchestration using Recovery Plans</a> feature available in Azure Site Recovery. Recovery plans make failover and failback from Azure easy and ensure that you meet your Recovery Time Objectives (RTO) goals of your organization.  <p>Check out additional <a href=\"http://aka.ms/b2a_blog_pricing\">pricing</a> or <a href=\"http://aka.ms/b2a_blog_productinfo\">product information</a> about Azure Site Recovery, and <a href=\"http://aka.ms/b2a_blog_trial\">sign up for a free Azure trial</a> and start using it today.  <h2><u>Active Directory: GA of Application Proxy and Password Writeback support</u></h2> <p>Today's Azure update includes some great updates to Azure Active Directory.  <h4><em><u>Azure Active Directory Application Proxy </u></em></h4> <p>The Azure Active Directory Application Proxy allows you to make your on-premises web applications securely accessible to users who want to use them from the cloud - and enables you to authenticate access to them using Azure AD.  <p>You can do this without changing your applications and without having to change your DMZ configuration. Just install a lightweight connector anywhere on your network and configure access to the application in your Azure Active Directory, and you can make your SharePoint, Outlook Web Access (or any other Web application that relies on Kerberos) available to users outside your corporate network.  <p><a href=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/a2f3e6cdd02d_1280A/image_18.png\"><img title=\"image\" style=\"border-left-width: 0px; border-right-width: 0px; border-bottom-width: 0px; display: inline; border-top-width: 0px\" border=\"0\" alt=\"image\" src=\"https://aspblogs.blob.core.windows.net/media/scottgu/WindowsLiveWriter/a2f3e6cdd02d_1280A/image_thumb_8.png\" width=\"540\" height=\"254\"></a>  <p>With today's release we added support for Kerberos Constrained Delegation. Now, once a user has authenticated to Azure Active Directory, the Azure Active Directory Application Proxy can automatically authenticate users to your on-premises application.  <h4><em><u>Password Writeback for Azure Active Directory Premium Customers</u></em></h4> <p>With the new Password Writeback support in Azure AD Sync, you can now configure your Active Directory system so that any time a user or administrator changes a password in Azure AD, the new password is also written back to your on-premises Active Directory as well. So, for example, when a user forgets their password to your on-premises AD, they can reset their password using the Azure AD password reset service we provide in the cloud, and then use their new password to sign on to your on-premises AD.&nbsp; This makes it easier for organizations to enable a variety of self-service IT and password reset features to their employees and partners.  <h4><em><u>Preview of security questions for password reset</u></em></h4> <p>With today's release we’re also introducing preview support that enables you to configure security questions for password reset scenarios. This enables users to register their answers to secret questions, and then use those answers to prove who they are when they go to reset a forgotten password.  <h4><em><u>Add your own password SSO for SaaS applications</u></em></h4> <p>With today's release we are introducing the preview of functionality that lets you configure password-based single sign-on for any web application that has an HTML sign-in page, even for applications that are not in the <a href=\"http://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/marketplace/active-directory/#all\">Azure AD Application Gallery</a>. You can also add any links to your users’ <a href=\"http://msdn.microsoft.com/en-us/library/azure/dn308588.aspx\">Azure AD Access Panel</a>, such as deep links to specific SharePoint pages, or to web apps that use Active Directory Federation Services.  <h4><em><u>More Ways to Get AD Premium</u></em></h4> <p>We now support the ability to purchase Azure Active Directory Premium online at the <a href=\"https://portal.office.com/commerce/catalog.aspx\">Office 365 commerce catalogue</a>, where you can purchase Azure AD Premium licenses for as many users as you want.&nbsp; You can then easily manage your Azure Active Directory by navigating to <a href=\"http://aka.ms/accessAAD\">http://aka.ms/accessAAD</a> or through the Office administration portal.<u></u>  <p>To learn more about these new capabilities and how you can start using them, read Alex Simons’ post on the <a href=\"http://blogs.technet.com/b/ad/\">Active Directory Team Blog</a>.  <h2><u>Summary</u></h2> <p>Today’s Microsoft Azure release enables a ton of great new scenarios, and makes building applications hosted in the cloud even easier.  <p>If you don’t already have a Azure account, you can sign-up for a <a href=\"https://www.windowsazure.com/en-us/pricing/free-trial/\">free trial</a> and start using all of the above features today.&nbsp; Then visit the <a href=\"https://azure.microsoft.com/\">Microsoft Azure Developer Center</a> to learn more about how to build apps with it.  <p>Hope this helps,  <p>Scott  <p><em>P.S.
